"Ajita, listen now. If there's beings who hear about the Buddha's lifespan being long like I just explained—if they can, even for one single thought-moment, generate faith and understanding—the merit they gonna get, that merit ain't got no limit. It can't be measured.

Now suppose there's a good man or a good woman who wants supreme perfect enlightenment, and for that goal they practice the Five Perfections for eighty myriads of millions of billions of nayutas of eons—

Let me tell you what that looks like:

GIVING: For all those eons, giving gifts. Giving to Buddhas, giving to solitary realizers, giving to Bodhisattvas. Giving precious and wonderful food and drink. Giving the finest clothes and bedding. Building temples out of sandalwood. Creating parks and gardens to make them beautiful. All kinds of giving, every kind wonderful and fine, through all those countless eons, dedicating it all toward the Buddha Way.

KEEPING PRECEPTS: Pure ethical conduct, clean and without a crack or leak, seeking the supreme path, the kind of conduct all Buddhas praise.

PATIENCE: Practicing forbearance, dwelling in that gentle, flexible ground. Even when all kinds of evil people come attacking, adding insults and harm, the mind don't tilt, don't tip over, don't move. Even when people who got a little bit of the Dharma come at you with their arrogance, looking down on you and troubling you—you can bear that too.

DILIGENT EFFORT: Vigorously progressing, your intention and mindfulness always solid and firm, for immeasurable hundreds of millions of eons, single-minded, never resting, never slacking off even once.

MEDITATION: Living for countless eons in quiet, empty places, whether sitting or walking, always—except when sleeping—keeping your mind collected and controlled. And because of this, producing all the meditations and concentrations, stable and unshaken in mind for eighty hundreds of millions of eons.

Taking all this one-pointed meditative merit and using it to seek the supreme path. Getting all the wisdom, mastering all the meditation states.

For hundreds and thousands of millions and billions of eons, this person practices all these meritorious virtues just like I described.

But then—

If there's a good man or good woman who hears me speak about my lifespan and believes it for even ONE SINGLE THOUGHT-MOMENT—

The blessing they get EXCEEDS all that other merit.

It ain't even close.

Not one part in a hundred. Not one part in a thousand. Not one part in hundreds of thousands of millions of billions. Can't even calculate the comparison. Can't make the numbers work. The metaphors fail.

If a good man or good woman has this kind of merit from believing—
Impossible they gonna retreat from supreme enlightenment.
Can't happen.
No such place exists where that could occur."

## THE BUDDHA SPEAKS IT IN VERSE

Then the World-Honored One, wanting to speak this meaning again, said in verse:

*If someone seeking Buddha wisdom*
*For eighty myriads of millions of billions*
*Of nayuta eons*
*Practices the Five Perfections—*

*During all those eons,*
*Giving offerings to Buddhas,*
*To solitary realizers and their disciples,*
*And to Bodhisattva assemblies—*

*Precious and wonderful food and drink,*
*Fine clothing and bedding,*
*Building sandalwood temples,*
*Decorating them with gardens and groves—*

*All this kind of giving,*
*Various and wonderful in every way,*
*Through all those eons,*
*Dedicating it to the Buddha Way—*

*If they also keep the precepts,*
*Pure and clean, without crack or leak,*
*Seeking the supreme path,*
*The kind all Buddhas praise and speak—*

*If they also practice patience,*
*Dwelling on that ground of gentle adjustment,*
*Even when crowds of evil come attacking,*
*Their mind don't incline, don't make that judgment—*

*And when those who got a little Dharma,*
*Holding on to their prideful ways,*
*Look down and trouble this patient one,*
*Still able to endure throughout their days—*

*If they also diligently progress,*
*Their will and mindfulness constantly firm and strong,*
*For immeasurable hundreds of millions of eons*
*Single-minded, never lazy for long—*

*And for countless eons more,*
*Dwelling in quiet and empty places,*
*Whether sitting or walking,*
*Except for sleep, always gathering their mental spaces—*

*And because of this,*
*Able to produce all those meditation states,*
*For eighty hundreds of millions of eons*
*Dwelling in mental stability, mind that concentrates—*

*Holding this one-pointed blessing,*
*Seeking the supreme Way in their heart,*
*Saying: 'I will get all-wisdom,*
*Exhaust all meditative arts'—*

*This person, for hundreds and thousands*
*And millions and billions of eons,*
*Practices all these meritorious virtues*
*Like I just described with all these reasons—*

*But if there's good men or women*
*Who hear me speak about my lifespan,*
*And believe it even for one thought-moment,*
*Their blessing exceeds that other plan.*

*If a person completely without*
*Any doubt or regret at all,*
*Believes with deep mind even briefly,*
*Their blessing is like this—so tall.*

*Those Bodhisattvas who,*
*For immeasurable eons, walked the Way,*
*Hearing me speak about my lifespan,*
*They can believe and accept what I say.*

*People like this*
*Receive this scripture on the crown of their head,*
*Making this vow: 'In the future,*
*May I have long life and leave none unfed.*

*Just like the World-Honored One today,*
*King among the Shakya clan,*
*Lion-roaring in the place of enlightenment,*
*Speaking Dharma fearless—that's my plan.*

*We, in the worlds to come,*
*Honored and respected by everyone there,*
*When sitting in the place of enlightenment,*
*Will speak about lifespan in the same way—with care.'*

*If there are those with deep mind,*
*Pure and straightforward and true,*
*Much learning and able to retain it,*
*Understanding Buddha's words according to their cue—*

*People like this*
*About this teaching have no doubt."

## WHAT DEEP FAITH LOOKS LIKE

"Furthermore, Ajita, if someone hears about the Buddha's long lifespan and understands what it's getting at, the merit that person gets got no limit. They can arouse the Tathāgata's supreme wisdom.

How much more so if they widely hear this scripture, or teach others to hear it, or hold it themselves, or teach others to hold it, or write it themselves, or teach others to write it, or make offerings to the scripture scroll with flowers, incense, necklaces, banners, canopies, silk hangings, fragrant oils and butter lamps—that person's merit is immeasurable and boundless. It can produce the wisdom that knows all kinds.

Ajita, if a good man or good woman hears me speak about my long lifespan and believes it with deep mind and understanding—then they seeing the Buddha constantly present on Vulture Peak Mountain, surrounded by the great Bodhisattvas and the assembly of hearers, speaking the Dharma.

And more: they seeing this Saha world, how the ground is lapis lazuli, level and even and smooth. The roads marked out with Jambu-river gold in eight directions. Jeweled trees standing in rows. Towers and pavilions all made of jewels. And the assembly of Bodhisattvas dwelling right there in them.

If someone can see like this, you should know: this is the sign of deep faith and understanding.

## EVEN JUST NOT REJECTING IT

Furthermore, after the Tathāgata passes into extinction, if someone hears this scripture and don't tear it down, don't speak against it, but just feels a little joy rise up in their heart—you should know: this already is the sign of deep faith and understanding.

How much more so someone who reads and recites it, who receives and holds it—that person carrying the Tathāgata on top of their head.

Ajita, this good man or good woman don't need to build stupas or temples for me, don't need to construct monks' quarters or make the fourfold offering to the monastic community.

Why not?

Because a good man or good woman who receives, holds, reads, and recites this scripture—they already raised up a stupa, already built the monks' quarters, already made offering to the community.

It means they already raised up a seven-jeweled stupa over the Buddha's relics—tall and wide, tapering smaller as it rises up to Brahma Heaven, with banners and canopies hanging from it and many jeweled bells, with flowers and incense and necklaces, with powdered incense and paste incense and burning incense, with drums and music, with flutes and pipes and harps, with all kinds of dancing and performance, with wonderful sound and voice singing praises—and they already been making this offering for immeasurable thousands and myriads and hundreds of millions of eons.

## THE INVISIBLE MONASTERY

Ajita, if after I pass into extinction, someone hears this scripture and can receive and hold it, whether writing it themselves or teaching others to write it—then they have built a monastery of thirty-two halls made of red sandalwood, each hall eight tala trees tall, high and wide and beautiful, with a hundred thousand monks dwelling there, with gardens and bathing pools, with walking paths and meditation caves, with robes and food and drink, with beds and bedding and medicine, with all kinds of joyful necessities filling it up completely. Monasteries and halls like this—hundreds and thousands and myriads and hundreds of millions of them, uncountably many—appearing right in front of them, making offering to me and to the community of monks.

So that's why I say: After the Tathāgata passes into extinction, if someone can receive, hold, read, recite, and speak this scripture for others, or write it themselves or teach others to write it, or make offerings to the scripture scroll—they don't need to build stupas or temples or construct monks' quarters or make offerings to the monastic community.

How much more so if someone can hold this scripture and also practice giving, keeping precepts, patience, diligent effort, single-mindedness, and wisdom—their virtue is supreme, immeasurable, boundless.

It's like empty space—east, west, south, north, the four intermediate directions, above, below—immeasurable and boundless.

That person's merit, likewise, is immeasurable and boundless like that.

They quickly arrive at the wisdom that knows all kinds.

If someone reads, recites, receives, and holds this scripture, speaks it for others, writes it themselves or teaches others to write it, and also can build stupas and construct monks' quarters, make offerings and praises to the community of hearers, and with hundreds of thousands of myriads of hundreds of millions of praising methods praise the merit of Bodhisattvas, and for other people, according to various causes and conditions, explains this Dharma Flower Scripture following its meanings, and also can purely keep the precepts, dwelling together with gentle and flexible people, patient and without anger, with firm will and mindfulness, always valuing sitting meditation and attaining deep meditations, vigorously brave and gathering in all good dharmas, with sharp faculties and wisdom, good at answering difficult questions—

## ALREADY AT THE TREE

Ajita, if after I pass into extinction, good men and good women who receive, hold, read, and recite this scripture also have these kinds of good meritorious virtues—you should know: this person already proceeding to the place of enlightenment, drawing near to supreme perfect enlightenment, sitting under the tree of the Way.

Ajita, wherever that good man or good woman sits, stands, or walks—right there a stupa should be built. All the gods and humans should make offerings to it like it's the Buddha's stupa."

## THE BUDDHA SPEAKS IT IN VERSE AGAIN

Then the World-Honored One, wanting to speak this meaning again, said in verse:

*If after I pass into extinction,*
*Someone can respectfully hold this scripture,*
*That person's blessing is immeasurable,*
*Like I explained up there for sure.*

*This means they completely fulfilled*
*All the various offerings made,*
*Raising up a stupa with relics,*
*Adorned with seven jewels displayed—*

*The pole reaching high and wide,*
*Tapering smaller up to Brahma's place,*
*Jeweled bells by the thousands and myriads of hundreds of millions,*
*Wind moving them with wonderful sound and grace.*

*And for immeasurable eons*
*Making offerings to this stupa tall,*
*With flowers and incense and many necklaces,*
*Heavenly clothes and music for all,*

*Burning fragrant oil and butter lamps,*
*Constantly illuminating all around.*
*In the evil age when Dharma's ending,*
*If someone can hold this scripture found—*

*It means they already, like I said above,*
*Completely fulfilled all the offerings made.*
*If someone can hold this scripture,*
*It's like the Buddha's still here, not yet decayed.*

*With ox-head sandalwood*
*Building monks' quarters as an offering place,*
*With thirty-two halls,*
*Each one eight tala trees high, full of grace—*

*Fine food and wonderful clothing,*
*Beds and bedding all fulfilled,*
*Hundreds and thousands dwelling there,*
*Gardens and bathing pools all built,*

*Walking paths and meditation caves,*
*Everything beautiful in various ways.*
*If someone with faithful, understanding mind*
*Receives, holds, reads, recites through their days,*

*Or also teaches others to write it,*
*And makes offerings to the scripture scroll,*
*Scattering flowers, incense, powdered incense,*
*With sumanas, champaka from the soul,*

*Atimuktaka flowers and fragrant oils*
*Constantly burning them bright—*
*One who makes offerings like this*
*Gets immeasurable merit and light.*

*Boundless as empty space,*
*So is their blessing likewise.*
*How much more so holding this scripture*
*While also giving, that's twice as wise—*

*And keeping precepts, patient, loving meditation,*
*Not angry, not speaking evil or mean,*
*Respectful toward stupas and temples,*
*Humble toward all monks seen,*

*Far away from prideful mind,*
*Always contemplating wisdom's way,*
*When questioned and challenged, not getting angry,*
*Following along to explain, to say—*

*If someone can practice this practice,*
*Their merit can't be measured.*
*If you see this Dharma teacher*
*Accomplished in virtue to be treasured,*

*You should scatter heavenly flowers on them,*
*Cover their body with heavenly clothes,*
*Touch your head to the ground at their feet,*
*Think of them as the Buddha—that's how it goes.*

*You should also make this thought:*
*'Before long they'll proceed to the place of the Way,*
*Attaining leakless and unconditioned truth,*
*Widely benefiting people and gods—both night and day.'*

*The place where they dwell and stay,*
*Where they walk or sit or lie,*
*Even if they speak just one verse there,*
*In that spot a stupa should rise high,*

*Adorned and made beautiful,*
*Offered to in various ways.*
*A child of Buddha dwelling on this ground—*
*This is the Buddha's place for all his days,*

*Constantly present right there within,*
*Walking around and sitting and lying down."

### END OF CHAPTER SEVENTEEN: COUNTING UP THE GRACE

*Blues Interpretation from Classical Chinese by Kumārajīva*

---

## INTERPRETATION NOTES:

This chapter is about the mathematics of grace—the impossible calculation that one moment of faith outweighs eons of effort. It's the scandal at the heart of the Dharma: you can work for billions of lifetimes doing everything right, or you can simply believe for one instant what the Buddha revealed in Chapter 16 (his eternal life), and that one instant of faith generates more merit.

The blues/gospel tradition knows this paradox well—salvation by grace, not by works; the last made first; the thief on the cross entering paradise that very day. The structure of this chapter—the counting, the comparison, the shock, the celebration—mirrors revival meeting testimonies where people try to count up what God has done and the numbers just keep climbing until words fail.

Key metaphors preserved:
- **Dust particles**: The traditional Buddhist way of counting the uncountable, here rendered plainly to let the accumulation itself create wonder
- **The invisible monastery**: What faith builds spiritually is more real than what hands build physically—a pure blues theology move
- **The stupa wherever they stand**: Sacred ground is made by sacred presence, not by construction projects
- **One thought-moment of faith**: The instant of belief that changes everything—conversion experience, moment of grace

The tone shifts between astonishment (the opening counting), celebration (heaven's response), instruction (Buddha's explanation), and prophetic recognition (you're already there, you just don't know it yet). All of these are familiar movements in blues/gospel expression, which regularly moves from testimony to praise to teaching to vision within a single song or sermon.

The repetition of "as many as dust particles" functions like the repetitive counting in spirituals and gospel songs—"ten thousand angels," "million years," "all God's children"—where the piling up of large numbers creates a sense of abundance beyond grasping, grace beyond measuring.

# CHAPTER EIGHTEEN: THE JOY THAT MULTIPLIES

*Blues Interpretation from Classical Chinese by Kumārajīva*
(隨喜功德品第十八 - The Merit of Rejoicing and Passing It On)

Blues/Gospel Interpretation from Kumārajīva's Classical Chinese (406 CE)
Rendered into vernacular English

## THE QUESTION ABOUT PASSING IT ON

Right then, Maitreya Bodhisattva stood up and asked the Buddha:

"World-Honored One, if there's a good man or a good woman who hears this Lotus Sutra and their heart just REJOICES—I mean really rejoices, gets happy about it, feels that joy rise up in them—how much blessing they gonna get? What kind of merit comes from that simple joy?"

And then he spoke it in verse:

*After the World-Honored One passes on,*
*If someone hears this teaching here,*
*And they can just rejoice in it—*
*How much blessing does that bring near?*

## THE BUDDHA'S ANSWER: THE CHAIN OF TRANSMISSION

The Buddha turned to Maitreya and said:

"Ajita, listen here. After I'm gone—after the Tathāgata passes into extinction—if a monk or a nun, if a laywoman or a layman, if somebody with wisdom whether they old or they young, if they hear this sutra and they REJOICE in it, and then they leave that dharma assembly and go somewhere else—

Maybe they go to a monastery, maybe they go to some quiet empty place, maybe they in the city streets or the back alleys, maybe they in a village or out in the fields—

And they tell it. They tell what they heard.

They tell their mama and their daddy, they tell their kinfolk, they tell their friends and the people they know. They use whatever words they got, whatever strength they got, and they PASS IT ON.

And those people hear it and they rejoice too. And what do they do? They go and tell somebody else.

And that person hears it and rejoices, and they tell somebody else.

And it goes on like that, passing from hand to hand, from mouth to mouth, from heart to heart—

It keeps going, keeps spreading, keeps multiplying—

Until it reaches the FIFTIETH person in that chain.

Now Ajita, let me tell you about that fiftieth good man or good woman—the one at the end of that long line of telling. Let me tell you about the merit they get just from hearing and rejoicing.

Listen good to what I'm about to say."

## THE GREAT BENEFACTOR (THE COMPARISON)

"Imagine this:

Imagine there's four hundred million billion countless world systems. You can't even count that many worlds—more worlds than you got numbers for.

And in all those worlds, there's beings in the six realms—gods and humans, asuras and animals, hungry ghosts and hell-dwellers.

Every kind of birth: egg-born, womb-born, moisture-born, transformation-born.

Every kind of form: got form, don't got form.

Every kind of consciousness: got consciousness, don't got consciousness, got neither and got both.

Every kind of body: no feet, two feet, four feet, many feet.

All the beings there are—every single one that counts as a living creature—

Now imagine a person who wants to do good, who wants to create blessing. And they go to all those beings and they say: 'What you want? What brings you joy? What makes you happy?'

And whatever entertainment those beings desire, whatever pleasure items they want, this benefactor GIVES IT TO THEM. Gives it all.

And to each single being—every last one—they give gold and silver, lapis lazuli and mother-of-pearl, agate and coral and amber. All kinds of wonderful precious treasures.

And elephants. And horses. And carriages. And precious palanquins to ride in.

And palaces made of seven kinds of jewels. And towers. And pavilions.

To EACH being, they give enough to fill the whole continent of Jambudvīpa—that's this whole earth we're standing on. Each one gets that much treasure.

And this great benefactor keeps giving like this for EIGHTY YEARS.

Eighty years of constant giving.

Then after eighty years, that benefactor looks at all those beings and thinks:

'I done gave them everything for pleasure and entertainment, everything their hearts desired. But look at them now—they getting old. Already past eighty years old themselves, hair gone white, faces all wrinkled. They gonna die soon. Won't be long now.

I better teach them the Buddha's Dharma. I better train them in the truth before they go.'

So that benefactor gathers all those countless beings together and proclaims the Dharma to them. Teaches them, instructs them, benefits them, brings them joy.

And right then—all at one time—every single one of them attains the Way:

Some become stream-enterers (Śrotāpanna)—first step on the path.

Some become once-returners (Sakṛdāgāmin)—just one more birth to go.

Some become non-returners (Anāgāmin)—ain't coming back to this world no more.

Some become Arhats (Arahant)—completely done, fully free.

All of them eliminate every outflow, every leak of defilement.

All of them become masters of deep meditation, dwelling in profound samādhi.

All of them gain the eight liberations—free in every way there is to be free.

Now Ajita—what you think? You think that great benefactor got a lot of merit? You think they accumulated some blessings or what?"

## MAITREYA'S ANSWER

Maitreya said to the Buddha:

"World-Honored One, that person got merit beyond measure! Can't even count it, can't even number it.

I mean, if that benefactor had just GIVEN all those beings the pleasure items, the entertainment and joy—that alone would be merit without measure.

But you talking about they also led every single one of them to become an Arhat! That's merit on top of merit, blessing piled on blessing!"

## THE SHOCKING TRUTH

The Buddha said to Maitreya:

"Let me tell you straight and clear now. Let me break it down so there ain't no confusion:

That person who gave all those pleasure items to beings in four hundred million billion countless world systems—

Who gave to beings in all six realms of existence—

Who gave for eighty solid years—

And then led every single one of them to become Arhats, to attain complete liberation—

All that merit, all that blessing, all that good karma—

Don't equal the merit of that FIFTIETH person who heard just ONE VERSE of the Lotus Sutra and rejoiced.

You hear me?

The fiftieth person in the chain.

The one at the very end.

The last one to hear it.

Who just heard ONE VERSE.

And just REJOICED.

That person's merit is GREATER.

Not equal. GREATER.

The great benefactor's merit ain't even one hundredth part.

Not one thousandth part.

Not one hundred thousand million billionth part.

You can't calculate it. You can't number it. You can't use arithmetic to figure it. You can't use analogies to explain it.

There ain't no comparison.

Now Ajita, think about this:

If that fiftieth person—the LAST one in the chain, the one who heard it from someone who heard it from someone who heard it from someone forty-eight times removed from the source—

If THAT person's merit from just hearing one verse and rejoicing is already beyond measure, already infinite, already countless—

What about the forty-ninth person who told them?

What about the forty-eighth?

What about the person earlier in the chain?

What about the person earlier than that?

And what about the FIRST person—the one who heard it right there in the dharma assembly and rejoiced?

That person's blessing is even MORE beyond compare. More infinite than infinite. More countless than countless.

Can't be measured at all."

## THE BLESSINGS OF SMALL ACTS

"And listen, Ajita—let me tell you more:

If someone goes to a monastery to hear this sutra—

Even if they just SIT there for a moment—

Even if they just STAND there for a moment—

Even if they only listen for a brief instant—

Because of that merit, in their next life they gonna be born and receive:

Fine excellent elephants, fine excellent horses, fine excellent carriages, precious jeweled palanquins to ride in. They gonna even ride in heavenly palaces up in the god realms.

And if someone's at a place where this Dharma is being taught, and they're sitting down listening—

And another person comes along—

And the first person encourages that newcomer: 'Sit down and listen!'

Or maybe they share their own seat, move over to make room so the other person can sit and listen—

Because of that merit, in their next life they gonna be born and receive:

The seat of Indra, king of the gods.

Or the seat of Brahma, lord of this world.

Or the seat of a wheel-turning sacred king, ruler of the four continents.

Just from offering a seat. Just from making room. Just from saying 'Sit down, listen here.'"

## THE BEAUTIFUL MOUTH THAT SPEAKS DHARMA

"And Ajita, if someone says to another person:

'There's a sutra called the Lotus Dharma. Let's go listen to it together.'

And that person receives the teaching, accepts the invitation, and goes with them—

And they listen together, even if just for a brief moment—

Because of that merit, in their next life they gonna be born together with Dhāraṇī Bodhisattvas—wisdom-keepers, truth-holders.

And they gonna have:

Sharp faculties.
Keen wisdom.

For a hundred thousand million lifetimes, they won't never be mute. They won't never be dumb-struck. They gonna have speech.

Their mouth breath won't never stink.

Their tongue won't never be sick.

Their mouth won't never be diseased.

Their teeth won't be dirty.
Won't be black.
Won't be yellow.
Won't be sparse or missing teeth.
Won't have gaps.
Won't be crooked.
Won't be broken.

Their lips won't hang down low.
Won't be shriveled up.
Won't be thick and rough.
Won't have sores or blemishes.
Won't be damaged.
Won't be twisted to the side.
Won't be thick.
Won't be too big.
Won't be dark.
Won't have anything ugly about them.

Their nose won't be flat.
Won't be crooked.

Their face won't be dark-colored.
Won't be too long and narrow.
Won't be sunken in or twisted.
Won't have a single feature that ain't pleasant to look at.

Their lips, tongue, and teeth gonna be perfectly beautiful.

Their nose gonna be refined, high, and straight.

Their face gonna be round and full.

Their eyebrows gonna be high and long.

Their forehead gonna be broad, flat, and perfectly proportioned.

All their human features gonna be complete and perfect.

Life after life, wherever they born, they gonna see Buddhas and hear the Dharma and receive the teaching with faith."

## THE ESCALATION OF MERIT

"Now Ajita, just LOOK at this:

Just from encouraging ONE person to go listen to the Dharma—the merit is already like this, already beyond measure.

So what about someone who listens with a whole mind, with full attention?

What about someone who not only listens but EXPLAINS it, TEACHES it, interprets it and breaks it down for other people?

What about someone who not only hears it and teaches it but PRACTICES it, LIVES it, does exactly what it says?

That merit can't be measured at all. Can't even begin to calculate it."

## THEN THE BUDDHA SANG IT

Right then the World-Honored One, wanting to drive this truth home one more time, spoke in verse:

*If someone at a dharma gathering*
*Hears this sutra here,*
*Even just one single verse,*
*And rejoices when they hear,*

*Then goes and teaches it to others,*
*Passes it on down the line,*
*Until it reaches the fiftieth person—*
*That last person's merit gonna shine.*

*Now let me break down and distinguish*
*What that last person gonna receive:*
*Imagine a great benefactor giving—*
*More than your mind can conceive.*

*They supply countless multitudes,*
*Give them everything they desire,*
*Keep on giving eighty years—*
*Never let that charity tire.*

*Then seeing those people getting old,*
*Hair white and faces all creased,*
*Teeth sparse and bodies dried up,*
*Death approaching from the east,*

*That benefactor thinks: 'Right now*
*I better teach them truth that's pure,*
*I better give them the Way to freedom,*
*Help them find what will endure.'*

*So they teach them the dharma lovingly,*
*Teach them about nirvāṇa's real law,*
*Say: 'This world ain't solid at all,*
*Like water bubbles, foam, and straw—*

*Like flames flickering, shadows passing—*
*Y'all better develop detachment quick,*
*Better grow that mind that sees through illusion,*
*Before time runs out and you caught in the trick.'*

*All those people hearing this teaching*
*Every one becomes an Arhat true,*
*Possessing six spiritual powers,*
*Three knowledges and eight liberations too.*

*But that fiftieth person in the chain*
*Who just heard one verse and felt joy—*
*THAT person's blessing exceeds all that giving,*
*Can't be compared, can't be measured by no ploy.*

*So if the person at the END of the chain*
*Gets merit beyond all measuring—*
*What about those earlier in the line?*
*What about the FIRST person rejoicing and believing?*

## THE SPECIFIC BLESSINGS OF INVITATION

*If someone encourages just one person,*
*Brings them along to hear the Lotus taught,*
*Saying 'This sutra is deep and wonderful,*
*Hard to encounter in a thousand million ages' worth of thought—*

*And that person receives the teaching,*
*Accepts the invitation to come hear,*
*Even if they only listen a moment—*
*Let me tell you the blessings that appear:*

*Life after life, no trouble with their mouth,*
*Teeth won't be sparse or yellow or black,*
*Lips won't be thick or shriveled or damaged,*
*Nothing ugly, nothing that others would attack.*

*Tongue won't be dry or black or short,*
*Nose gonna be high and refined and straight,*
*Forehead broad and perfectly level,*
*Face and features handsome and great.*

*They gonna be somebody people love to see,*
*Mouth breath won't never be foul,*
*The fragrance of the blue lotus flower*
*Gonna come out their mouth right now.*

## THE BLESSINGS OF SIMPLY SHOWING UP

*If they deliberately go to the monastery*
*Wanting to hear the Lotus Sutra read,*
*And they listen even a moment with joy—*
*Let me tell you where that blessing gonna lead:*

*Next life they born among gods and humans,*
*They gonna receive wonderful elephant, horse, and cart,*
*Precious jeweled palanquins to ride in,*
*Even riding in the heavenly palace to take part.*

*If at a place where Dharma's being taught*
*They encourage someone to sit and hear,*
*Because of that blessed connection—*
*Indra's seat, Brahma's seat, or the wheel-king's gonna appear.*

## THE FINAL QUESTION

*So what about someone who listens with whole mind,*
*Who explains the meaning and the sense,*
*Who practices exactly what it teaches?*
*THAT blessing is beyond immense!*

### END OF CHAPTER EIGHTEEN: THE JOY THAT MULTIPLIES

*Blues Interpretation from Classical Chinese by Kumārajīva*

---

## INTERPRETATION NOTES:

This chapter is about viral transmission before there was such a thing—about how truth spreads from person to person like fire, like news, like a song everybody needs to hear. The Buddha's teaching here is mathematical and mystical at once: merit doesn't just add, it MULTIPLIES. It grows exponentially with each telling.

The shocking comparison is the heart of it: the greatest material generosity in the universe (giving everything to everyone for eighty years PLUS leading them all to Arhat-hood) is LESS than the merit of the fiftieth person who just heard a verse and felt joy. Why? Because the Lotus Sutra itself IS the teaching that leads to Buddhahood—not just to Arhat-hood. It's the higher truth, the bigger vehicle. One verse of it carries more potential than all the arhats in all the worlds.

And notice the progression of blessings:
 you get treasure in the next life
 you get a throne in the next life
 you get a beautiful body and you meet Buddhas forever

The "beautiful mouth" passage is profound: the mouth that speaks Dharma becomes beautiful because it's doing what mouths were made for—speaking truth, passing on liberation. Form follows function. The body that serves the teaching becomes perfected by that service.

This is word-of-mouth gospel. This is "each one teach one." This is the mathematics of grace: one person tells one person tells one person, and fifty tellings later, the last person in the chain has more blessing than the richest philanthropist who ever lived.

Pass it on.

# CHAPTER NINETEEN: WHEN YOUR SENSES WAKE UP

*Blues Interpretation from Classical Chinese by Kumārajīva*
(法師功德品第十九 - The Merit of the Dharma Teacher)

Blues/Gospel Interpretation from Kumārajīva's Classical Chinese (406 CE)
Rendered into vernacular English

## THE BUDDHA SPEAKS TO CONSTANT EXERTION

Right then, the Buddha turned to Constant-Exertion Bodhisattva and said:

"Listen here now. If there's a good man or a good woman who holds this Lotus Sutra—I mean really holds it, reads it out loud, recites it, explains it to folks, or writes it down with their own hand—

That person gonna get EIGHT HUNDRED eye-merits.

They gonna get TWELVE HUNDRED ear-merits.

They gonna get EIGHT HUNDRED nose-merits.

They gonna get TWELVE HUNDRED tongue-merits.

They gonna get EIGHT HUNDRED body-merits.

They gonna get TWELVE HUNDRED mind-merits.

And all these merits gonna PURIFY their six senses—gonna make them clean and clear and new.

Now this good person—their eyes, just the plain eyes their mama and daddy gave them, their regular flesh-and-blood eyes—they gonna see clear through the whole three-thousand-world system:

All the mountains inside and mountains outside,
All the forests, all the rivers, all the seas,
Down to the deepest hell (that's Avīci, the pit of no-interval suffering),
Up to the highest heaven (that's the Peak of Existence, where being goes as far as being goes).

And they gonna see all the beings in between.

They gonna see the karma that brought folks here.
They gonna see the causes and the effects.
They gonna see where beings gonna be born next and why.

They gonna see EVERYTHING. Know EVERYTHING.

All with the regular eyes they was born with."

## VERSE: SEEING WITH NEW EYES

Then the World-Honored One wanted to say it again in verse, so he spoke:

*If in a great assembly,*
*With a heart that ain't afraid,*
*You speak this Lotus Sutra—*
*Listen to the merit you done made.*

*That person gets eight hundred*
*Superior merits for the eye,*
*And with this decoration,*
*Their vision's purified.*

*With the eyes their parents gave them,*
*They see the whole three-thousand sphere—*
*The inner and the outer mountains,*
*Mount Sumeru standing clear,*

*The Iron Ring and all the rest,*
*The forests and the mountain wood,*
*The oceans and the flowing rivers,*
*Down to where the hell-fires burn for good,*

*Up to the Peak of Existence,*
*The highest place a being goes—*
*All creatures living in between,*
*Everything there is, they knows.*

*Though they ain't got the heavenly eye yet,*
*Their flesh-eye power's just like this—*
*Seeing clear through everything,*
*Nothing that their vision gonna miss.*

## EARS THAT HEAR EVERYTHING

"Now listen, Constant-Exertion. If a good man or a good woman holds this sutra, reads it, recites it, explains it, writes it down—

They gonna get TWELVE HUNDRED ear-merits.

And with those purified ears, they gonna hear EVERY SOUND in the whole three-thousand-world system:

Down to Avīci hell, up to the Peak of Existence, inside and outside, every kind of sound and voice—

Elephant sounds, horse sounds, ox sounds, chariot sounds.

Crying sounds and grieving sounds and sighing sounds.

Conch-shell sounds, drum sounds, bell sounds, chime sounds.

Laughing sounds and talking sounds.

Male voices, female voices, boy voices, girl voices.

Dharma sounds (that's truth-speaking).
Non-dharma sounds (that's lie-speaking).

Suffering sounds, pleasure sounds.

Common folks' sounds, holy people sounds.

Joy sounds, sorrow sounds.

Heaven sounds.
Dragon sounds.
Night-demon (yakṣa) sounds.
Gandharva sounds (that's the music-spirits).
Asura sounds (that's the fighting-titans).
Garuda sounds (that's the great birds).
Kiṃnara sounds (that's the song-spirits).
Mahoraga sounds (that's the great serpents).

Fire crackling. Water rushing. Wind blowing.

Hell-screams. Animal cries. Hungry-ghost moaning.

Monks chanting. Nuns reciting.

Śrāvaka voices (that's the hearers).
Pratyekabuddha voices (that's the solitary realizers).
Bodhisattva voices.
Buddha voices.

To sum it up quick: EVERY SOUND in the three-thousand-world system—every sound inside and every sound outside—

Even though they ain't got the heavenly ear yet, just with the regular ears their mama and daddy gave them, the clean natural ears they was born with—

They hear it ALL.

They can tell one sound from another.
They understand what everything means.

And their ears don't break. Don't get damaged. Don't go deaf from all that listening.

That's what holding this sutra does."

## VERSE: HEARING ALL THE VOICES

Then the World-Honored One spoke in verse:

*With the ears their parents gave them,*
*Clean and pure without no stain,*
*With these ordinary, common ears,*
*They hear the three-thousand-world domain.*

*Elephant, horse, carriage, cattle,*
*Bell and chime and conch and drum,*
*Zither, harp and lute sounds,*
*Flute and pipe—when music come,*

*Pure and lovely singing voices—*
*They listen but don't get attached.*
*Countless kinds of human speaking,*
*They hear and understand the batch.*

*And they hear the heaven-voices,*
*Subtle music, wondrous song,*
*Male and female speaking,*
*Boy and girl voices going strong.*

*In mountain canyons, dangerous valleys,*
*The kalavinka bird that sings,*
*The jīvaṃjīvaka and others—*
*They hear all these feathered things.*

*In the hells where beings suffer,*
*All the tortured, painful cries,*
*Hungry ghosts pressed by thirst and hunger,*
*Seeking food with desperate sighs,*

*The asuras and their families*
*Living by the great sea-shore,*
*When they speaking to each other,*
*Making voices loud that roar—*

*The dharma-speaker sitting here*
*Safe and settled in this place,*
*Can hear all these distant sounds*
*Without their ears losing grace.*

*In the ten-direction world systems,*
*Where birds and beasts call out their name,*
*The dharma-speaking person*
*Hears every creature all the same.*

*In the Brahma Heaven high above,*
*The Light-Sound and All-Pure sphere,*
*Up to the Peak of Existence,*
*Every word they speaking there—*

*The dharma teacher dwelling here*
*Can hear it all, can hear it true.*
*All the monks in assembly,*
*All the nuns reciting too—*

*Whether reading from the scriptures,*
*Whether teaching to the crowd—*
*The dharma teacher right here*
*Hears every word they speak out loud.*

*And all the Bodhisattvas*
*Reading sutras, studying dharma deep,*
*Teaching others, writing commentaries,*
*Explaining meanings—not one peep*

*Goes unheard by this dharma teacher.*
*The Buddhas—those Great Holy Ones—*
*Teaching beings, guiding creatures,*
*In great assemblies, every one,*

*Speaking subtle, wondrous teachings—*
*The one who holds this Lotus here*
*Hears every single dharma,*
*Every Buddha-word comes clear.*

*In the three-thousand-world system,*
*Every sound outside and in,*
*Down to Avīci suffering,*
*Up to where the heavens begin—*

*They hear every voice and sound*
*Without their hearing getting broke.*
*Their ears are sharp and sensitive,*
*Can tell apart each kind of folk.*

*The one who holds this Lotus Sutra,*
*Though they ain't got the heavenly ear,*
*Just using what they born with—*
*The merit's already right here.*

## NOSE THAT SMELLS EVERYTHING

"Now again, Constant-Exertion. If a good man or a good woman holds this sutra, reads it, recites it, explains it, writes it down—

They gonna complete EIGHT HUNDRED nose-merits.

And with that purified nose-root, they gonna smell EVERY SCENT in the three-thousand-world system—up and down, inside and outside, every kind of fragrance:

Sumana flower scent (that's jasmine).
Jāti flower scent (that's champak).
Mallikā flower scent (that's Arabian jasmine).
Campaka flower scent.
Pāṭala flower scent.

Red lotus scent. Blue lotus scent. White lotus scent.

Flowering tree scent. Fruit tree scent.

Sandalwood scent.
Agarwood scent (that's aloeswood).
Tamālapatra scent.
Tagara scent.

A thousand, ten-thousand kinds of mixed incense—
Whether powder incense, whether pellet incense, whether smearing incense—

The person holding this sutra, sitting right here in this spot, can tell them all apart.

And they can smell beings too:

Elephant scent, horse scent, ox scent, sheep scent.
Man scent, woman scent, boy scent, girl scent.

The smell of grass and trees and thickets and forests—whether near or whether far—all the scents that are, they smell them. Separate them out. Don't get it wrong.

The person holding this sutra, though they living right here, they also smell the heaven-scents:

The Pārijātaka tree scent (that's the coral tree).
The Kovidāra tree scent.
Mandārava flower scent.
Mahā-mandārava flower scent.
Mañjūṣaka flower scent.
Mahā-mañjūṣaka flower scent.
Sandalwood, agarwood, all kinds of powder incense,
All kinds of flower incense mixing together—

Heaven-incense combined in its fragrance—they know it, they don't miss nothing.

And they smell the bodies of the heaven-beings:

Indra (that's Śakra, the king of the gods) sitting in his Victory Hall, enjoying the five pleasures, playing around—they smell that.

When he in the Wonderful Dharma Hall teaching the Thirty-Three Gods—they smell that.

When he playing in the celestial gardens—they smell that.

All the other gods, male and female—they smell all their body-scents too.

And it keeps going up, turning and rising, all the way to the Brahma realm, up to the Peak of Existence—

All the heaven-beings' body-scents, they smell them all.

And they smell the incense the heaven-folk are burning too.

And they smell the śrāvakas' scent.
The pratyekabuddhas' scent.
The Bodhisattvas' scent.
The Buddhas' body-scent.

They smell it all from far away. They know exactly where each one is.

And even though they smelling all this, their nose don't get damaged. Don't get broke. Don't get confused.

If they want to tell somebody else, want to explain what they smelling—they remember it perfect. Don't get it wrong."

## VERSE: SMELLING THE WHOLE WORLD

Then the World-Honored One spoke in verse:

*This person's nose is purified—*
*In this world where we all live,*
*Whether fragrance, whether stinking,*
*Every kind of smell there is,*

*Sumana and jāti flowers,*
*Tamāla, sandalwood as well,*
*Agarwood and cinnamon,*
*All kinds of fruit and flower smell,*

*And they know the scent of beings—*
*Man scent, woman scent they find.*
*The dharma-speaker living distant*
*Smells the scent and knows their mind.*

*Great wheel-turning kings and lesser,*
*Their sons and all the court inside,*
*Ministers and palace women—*
*Smelling tells where they reside.*

*The precious things adorning bodies,*
*Treasures buried in the ground,*
*The jewel-women of wheel-turners—*
*By scent they know where they are found.*

*All the ornaments folks wearing,*
*Clothing, beads and necklace-chains,*
*All the different ointments smeared—*
*By smell they know from whom it came.*

*When heavenly beings walk or sit,*
*When they playing or they change their shape,*
*The one who holds this Lotus Sutra*
*Smelling knows, don't make mistake.*

*The flowering and fruiting trees,*
*The butter-oil and ghee perfume—*
*The sutra-holder sitting here*
*Knows where everything's in bloom.*

*In deep mountains, dangerous passes,*
*When sandalwood trees flower bright,*
*And beings dwelling in those places—*
*By smell they know them all on sight.*

*In the Iron Ring Mountain, the great sea,*
*Underground where creatures dwell—*
*The sutra-holder, by the fragrance,*
*Knows exactly where they dwell.*

*Asura men and women,*
*All their retinue and kin,*
*When they fighting, when they playing—*
*By smell they know the scene they're in.*

*In the wild and dangerous places,*
*Lions, elephants, tigers, wolves,*
*Buffalo and water-buffalo—*
*By smell they know where each one roams.*

*If there's a woman pregnant,*
*Can't tell yet if it's girl or boy,*
*If it's no-gender or non-human—*
*By smell they know what she'll enjoy.*

*By the power of smelling-knowledge,*
*They know the first time pregnancy take,*
*Whether it'll reach completion,*
*Whether she'll deliver safe, a blessed child she'll make.*

*By the power of smelling-knowledge,*
*They know what men and women thinking—*
*Lustful thoughts or angry, foolish,*
*Or if they practicing virtue, not sinking.*

*Underground where treasures hidden—*
*Gold and silver, precious stones,*
*Copper vessels holding riches—*
*By smell they find what's lying lone.*

*All kinds of beads and necklaces*
*That nobody can price or measure—*
*By smell they know if they expensive,*
*Where they from, where hides the treasure.*

*Heaven-flowers up above—*
*Mandārava, mañjūṣaka blooms,*
*The Pārijātaka tree—*
*By smell they know each flower's perfume.*

*Heaven-palaces above,*
*Whether high or middle, whether low they fall,*
*Adorned with precious jewels and flowers—*
*By smell they know them, one and all.*

*Heaven-gardens, splendid halls,*
*Fine pavilions, dharma towers standing tall,*
*Where beings sport and take their pleasure—*
*By smell they know it all.*

*When heavenly beings listening to dharma,*
*When they enjoying the five desires complete,*
*Coming, going, walking, sitting, lying down—*
*By smell they know it all, concrete.*

*The robes the heaven-women wearing,*
*Fine flowers, incense, ornaments so fair,*
*When they moving in their circle-dancing—*
*By smell they know it everywhere.*

*Like this, turning, rising upward,*
*All the way to Brahma's sphere,*
*Those entering samādhi, those emerging—*
*By smell they know who's sitting there.*

*Light-Sound Heaven, All-Pure Heaven,*
*Up to the Peak of Existence, the highest floor—*
*First birth and final falling-away—*
*By smell they know the whole life-score.*

*All the monks in assembly,*
*Always pressing on in dharma-work,*
*Whether sitting, whether walking,*
*Reading and reciting, never shirk—*

*Or underneath the forest trees,*
*Concentrated, sitting in deep meditation—*
*The sutra-holder, by the fragrance,*
*Knows exactly their location.*

*Bodhisattvas, firm in purpose,*
*Sitting in meditation, reading texts, or when*
*They teaching dharma to the people—*
*By smell they know all this, amen.*

*In every direction, the World-Honored Ones,*
*Revered by everyone who live,*
*Pitying beings, teaching dharma—*
*By smell they know the teaching that they give.*

*Beings there before the Buddha,*
*Hearing sutras, hearts made glad,*
*Practicing according to the dharma—*
*By smell they know the good they've had.*

*Though they ain't yet got the Bodhisattva*
*No-outflow dharma-nature nose complete,*
*Still this sutra-holding person*
*First obtains this nose so sweet.*

## TONGUE THAT TASTES HEAVEN

"Now again, Constant-Exertion. If a good man or a good woman holds this sutra, reads it, recites it, explains it, writes it down—

They gonna get TWELVE HUNDRED tongue-merits.

Whether it's good stuff or bad stuff, whether it's beautiful or whether it's ugly, whether it's delicious or whether it ain't—all the bitter and sour things—

When they touch that person's tongue-root, it ALL TURNS INTO SUPREME FLAVOR.

It tastes like heaven-nectar. Ain't nothing that don't taste good.

And if they use their tongue to speak in a great assembly, they gonna bring forth a DEEP AND SUBTLE VOICE that enters people's hearts. Makes everybody joyful and delighted.

And the heaven-sons and heaven-daughters—Indra, Brahmā, all the heaven-folk—when they hear this deep, subtle sound-voice speaking and teaching with its orderly words, they ALL COME TO LISTEN.

And the dragons and dragon-daughters,
The yakṣas and yakṣa-daughters,
The gandharvas and gandharva-daughters,
The asuras and asura-daughters,
The garuḍas and garuḍa-daughters,
The kiṃnaras and kiṃnara-daughters,
The mahoragas and mahoraga-daughters—

They all come near to listen to the dharma. Come close. Show respect. Make offerings.

And the monks, the nuns, the laymen, the laywomen.

Kings, princes, ministers, retinues.

Small wheel-turning kings, great wheel-turning kings, their seven treasures and thousand sons, inner and outer attendants—

They all ride up in their palace-carriages and come together to listen to the dharma.

Why? Because this Bodhisattva speaks the dharma WELL.

Brahmins, householders, people of the nation—all their life long, they stay close and make offerings.

And the śrāvakas, the pratyekabuddhas, the Bodhisattvas, the Buddhas—they always happy to see this person.

Wherever this person is, the Buddhas turn toward that direction to teach dharma.

They able to receive and hold ALL the Buddha-dharma.

And they able to bring forth the DEEP, SUBTLE DHARMA-SOUND."

## VERSE: SPEAKING WITH POWER

Then the World-Honored One spoke in verse:

*This person's tongue-root purified—*
*Never tastes no evil thing.*
*Whatever food they eating,*
*It all turns sweet, everything.*

*With deep, pure, subtle voice,*
*They preach the dharma to the crowd,*
*Using causes and conditions,*
*Using parables and metaphors told loud,*

*To guide the beings' hearts along.*
*All who hear become so glad,*
*They set out the best of offerings—*
*Give the finest gifts they ever had.*

*The heaven-folk—dragons, yakṣas,*
*Asuras and all the rest—*
*All with reverent, respectful hearts,*
*Come together as the blessed guest.*

*This dharma-speaking person—*
*If they want to, with sublime sound,*
*Fill up the three-thousand-world system—*
*Soon as they wish it, it resound.*

*Great and small wheel-turning kings,*
*Their thousand sons, their retinue complete,*
*With palms pressed together, reverent hearts,*
*Always coming to receive the teaching sweet.*

*Heaven-folk and dragons, yakṣas,*
*Rākṣasas and piśācas too,*
*Also with delighted hearts,*
*Always happy to make offerings new.*

*Brahmā the king, the Māra king,*
*Freedom Lord and Great Freedom one—*
*All these heaven-multitudes*
*Always coming where this teacher's throne.*

*All the Buddhas and disciples,*
*Hearing this one's dharma-sound,*
*Always mindful, always guarding,*
*Sometimes showing their form around.*

## BODY LIKE CRYSTAL MIRROR

"Now again, Constant-Exertion. If a good man or a good woman holds this sutra, reads it, recites it, explains it, writes it down—

They gonna get EIGHT HUNDRED body-merits.

They gonna get a PURE BODY—pure like clean lapis lazuli, like crystal glass.

Beings gonna LOVE to see a body like that.

And because their body so pure, the whole three-thousand-world system gonna show up in it:

When beings are born, when beings die,
Whether they born in good places or bad places,
Whether they high-quality or low-quality—

It all appears in that body.

And the Iron Ring Mountain, the Great Iron Ring Mountain, Mount Meru, Mahā-Meru Mountain, all the various mountains, and all the beings living in them—

They all appear in that body.

Down to Avīci hell, up to the Peak of Existence, all the places and all the beings—

They all appear in that body.

When the śrāvakas, the pratyekabuddhas, the Bodhisattvas, the Buddhas are teaching dharma—

They all appear in that body, showing their form and features."

## VERSE: THE MIRROR-BODY

Then the World-Honored One spoke in verse:

*If you hold the Lotus Sutra,*
*Your body becomes extremely pure—*
*Like that clean lapis lazuli—*
*Beings love to see for sure.*

*And like a bright, clean mirror*
*Reflecting every form that's there,*
*The Bodhisattva in their pure body*
*Sees everything the world can bear—*

*Only they understand it clearly,*
*Other folks can't see the same.*
*In the three-thousand-world system,*
*Every single living being's frame—*

*Heaven-folk and asuras,*
*Hell-dwellers, ghosts, and beasts that roam—*
*All these various forms and figures*
*Appear within that body-home.*

*All the heaven-palace dwellings,*
*Up to the Peak of Existence high,*
*The Iron Ring and Mount Meru,*
*Mahā-Meru reaching to the sky,*

*All the great sea-waters—*
*They all appear within that frame.*
*Buddhas and the śrāvaka-hearers,*
*Buddha-children, Bodhisattvas came—*

*Whether solitary, whether in assembly,*
*Teaching dharma—it all shows clear.*
*Though they ain't yet got the no-outflow*
*Dharma-nature wondrous body here,*

*With their pure and natural body,*
*Everything appears inside—*
*The whole creation in the mirror,*
*Nothing missing, nothing hide.*

## MIND THAT UNDERSTANDS EVERYTHING

"Now again, Constant-Exertion. If a good man or a good woman—after the Tathāgata's extinction—holds this sutra, reads it, recites it, explains it, writes it down—

They gonna get TWELVE HUNDRED mind-merits.

And with that purified mind-root, if they hear just ONE VERSE, just ONE SENTENCE—they gonna penetrate INFINITE, LIMITLESS meanings.

Once they understand these meanings, they able to speak on that one sentence, that one verse, for a month, for four months, even for a whole year.

And all the dharma they speak gonna accord with TRUE REALITY—ain't gonna contradict it.

If they speaking about worldly scriptures and books, about governing-the-world language, about making-a-living business matters—it's ALL gonna accord with the right dharma.

And the six-realm beings in the three-thousand-world system—whatever those beings are thinking in their minds, whatever their minds are doing, whatever their minds are playing around with—

This person KNOWS IT ALL.

Even though they ain't yet got the no-outflow wisdom, their mind-root is PURE LIKE THIS.

Whatever this person thinks about, whatever they calculate, whatever they say—

It's ALL Buddha-dharma. Ain't none of it not true.

It's also what the previous Buddhas taught in their sutras."

## VERSE: THE LUMINOUS MIND

Then the World-Honored One spoke in verse:

*This person's mind is purified,*
*Bright and sharp, without no stain.*
*With this wondrous mind-faculty,*
*They know the high and low and middle plain.*

*Hearing just a single verse,*
*They penetrate unlimited meaning-doors,*
*Then teach it step by step, according to the dharma—*
*One month, four months, even a year and more.*

*Inside this world and outside,*
*Every single being here—*
*Whether heaven-folk or dragons, whether human,*
*Yakṣas, ghosts, and spirits clear—*

*Those dwelling in the six life-courses,*
*All their countless thought-varieties—*
*As reward for holding the Lotus,*
*All at once they know these with ease.*

*The countless Buddhas in ten directions,*
*Adorned with hundred blessings, every mark,*
*Teaching dharma to the beings—*
*They hear it all and hold it in their heart.*

*Contemplating countless meanings,*
*Speaking dharma also without measure,*
*From beginning to the end, not forgetting, not mistaken—*
*This comes from holding Lotus treasure.*

*They know the characteristics of all dharmas,*
*Following the meaning, understanding sequence right,*
*Reaching into names and words and language—*
*Teaching just as they know it, bringing light.*

*Whatever this person speaks*
*Is all the dharma previous Buddhas taught.*
*And because they teach this dharma,*
*Before assemblies they ain't fraught.*

*The one who holds the Lotus Sutra—*
*Their mind-root pure exactly thus.*
*Though they ain't yet got no-outflow,*
*They got these marks already with us.*

*This person holding this sutra*
*Dwells securely in a rare place, blessed—*
*By all the beings*
*They joyfully loved and caressed.*

*Able to use a thousand, ten-thousand kinds*
*Of loving language manifold,*
*Distinguishing and teaching dharma—*
*This comes from holding Lotus, truth be told.*

### END OF CHAPTER NINETEEN: WHEN YOUR SENSES WAKE UP

*Blues Interpretation from Classical Chinese by Kumārajīva*
---

## INTERPRETATION NOTES:

This chapter is about TRANSFIGURATION OF THE SENSES. It ain't talking about gaining supernatural powers that separate you from ordinary life—it's talking about what happens when ordinary perception gets purified by holding the truth.

The blues has always known this: When you see clear, you see EVERYTHING. When you hear true, you hear EVERY VOICE—the suffering and the joy all mixed together. When you taste life after you've tasted grace, even the bitter turns to something you can swallow.

This chapter saying: The dharma don't take you OUT of the body—it wakes the body UP. It makes your eyes into telescopes, your ears into receivers, your nose into a compass, your tongue into a bell, your body into a mirror, your mind into a lamp.

You still using what your mama gave you. You still got the same flesh-and-blood senses you was born with. But now they PURIFIED. Now they AWAKE. Now they tell you the truth about what's really going on in this whole vast world.

And that's the merit—that's the blessing—that comes from HOLDING this sutra. From reading it, reciting it, explaining it, writing it down. From CARRYING this truth in your body and your life.

You want to see the whole world? You want to hear every voice? You want to know what folks are thinking, want to speak words that enter hearts, want your very body to become a mirror of all creation?

Then hold this dharma. Hold it close. Hold it true.

And your senses gonna wake up and tell you what's real.

# CHAPTER TWENTY: THE BODHISATTVA WHO NEVER LOOKED DOWN

*Blues Interpretation from Classical Chinese by Kumārajīva*
(常不輕菩薩品第二十)

A Blues Interpretation from Kumārajīva's Classical Chinese
The Wonderful Dharma Lotus Flower Sutra

## THE BUDDHA'S WORD TO GREAT POWER

Now the Buddha, he turned to that Bodhisattva Great Power - you know that Great Power, that Mahāsattva - and the Buddha said:

"Listen here now, you got to know this thing: When a monk or a nun, when a brother or a sister who holds fast to this Lotus teaching, when somebody come at them with a evil mouth, cursing them out, talking bad about them, slandering their name - oh, that somebody gonna reap a terrible harvest, like I done told you before. But the one who holds this teaching? They gonna gain merit, like I said - they gonna get them eyes cleaned up, ears purified, nose, tongue, body, mind all made clear and clean.

"Now Great Power, I'm gonna tell you about the ancient days. I'm talking way back, past counting, past measuring, past thinking about - we talking inconceivable, immeasurable ages ago, ages beyond ages. Back then there was a Buddha, and his name was King Sound-of-Thunder-and-Glory, the Tathāgata, the Worthy One, the One of Perfect Knowledge, Perfect in Understanding and Walking, Well-Gone, Knower of the World, Unsurpassed Teacher, Tamer of Strong Men, Teacher of Gods and Humans, the Buddha, the World-Honored One.

"That age was called the Age-Without-Decline. That country was called the Land of Great Achievement.

"That Buddha King Sound-of-Thunder-and-Glory, he taught the Dharma in that world to the gods and humans and the fighting demons. For them that was seeking to be disciples, he taught the Four Noble Truths - you know, about birth and old age and sickness and death, and how to cross over to final nirvāṇa. For them seeking to be solitary realizers, he taught the Twelve Links of Dependent Arising. For them Bodhisattvas seeking that supreme perfect enlightenment - that anuttara-samyak-sambodhi - he taught the Six Ways of Going to the Other Shore, the Six Perfections, so they could reach the Buddha's wisdom complete.

"Now Great Power, that Buddha King Sound-of-Thunder-and-Glory, he lived for four hundred thousand million billion nayutas of Ganges River sands of ages. And the True Dharma stood in that world for ages like the dust particles in one Jambudvipa world. And the Imitation Dharma stood for ages like the dust particles in all four continents put together.

"After that Buddha had done good for all living beings, he passed into extinction. And after both the True Dharma and the Imitation Dharma had done passed away, in that same country another Buddha appeared, and his name was King Sound-of-Thunder-and-Glory too - the Tathāgata, Worthy One, One of Perfect Knowledge, Perfect in Understanding and Walking, Well-Gone, Knower of the World, Unsurpassed Teacher, Tamer of Strong Men, Teacher of Gods and Humans, the Buddha, the World-Honored One.

"And like this, one after another, there came twenty thousand million Buddhas, all with that same name."

## THE STORY OF NEVER LOOKED DOWN

"Now after that first Buddha King Sound-of-Thunder-and-Glory had passed into extinction, after the True Dharma had done gone, in the time of the Imitation Dharma, there was monks full up with arrogance and pride, and they had great power in that world.

"And in that time there was one Bodhisattva monk, and his name was Never Looked Down.

"Now Great Power, you might be wondering: Why they call him Never Looked Down? Well, I'm gonna tell you. This monk, every single person he seen - whether it was a monk or a nun, whether it was a brother or a sister - he would bow down low to every one of them, bow down deep and praise them, and he would say these words:

"'I respect you deeply. I wouldn't dare look down on you. Why? Because all of you are walking the Bodhisattva way. Every one of you is gonna become a Buddha.'

"Now this monk, he didn't spend his time studying scriptures and chanting texts. All he did was bow down and praise folks. Even when he seen the four kinds of people way off in the distance, he would go out of his way to get to them, bow down deep, praise them, and say:

"'I wouldn't dare look down on you. All of you are gonna become Buddhas.'

"But among them four kinds of people, there was some who had angry hearts, hearts that wasn't clean. They would curse him out with evil mouths, saying: 'This ignorant monk! Where he come from? Going around saying he don't look down on us, giving us prophecies that we gonna become Buddhas! We don't need no false prophecies like that! We don't want nothing to do with your empty predictions!'

"This went on for many years. He was constantly being cursed at and abused. But he never got angry. He just kept saying: 'You gonna become a Buddha.'

"And when he would say these words, sometimes folks would take up sticks and clubs, tiles and stones, and throw them at him, beat on him. He would run away and stand at a distance. But even then, he would lift up his voice high and call out loud:

"'I wouldn't dare look down on you! All of you are gonna become Buddhas!'

"Because he kept on saying these words all the time, them arrogant monks and nuns and brothers and sisters, they gave him the name Never Looked Down."

## DEATH AND RESURRECTION THROUGH THE WORD

"Now when this monk was about to die, right there in the sky, in the empty air, he heard all twenty thousand myriads of millions of verses of the Lotus Sutra that Buddha King Sound-of-Thunder-and-Glory had taught before. He was able to receive and hold every verse. Right then and there, he got them purified eye-roots like I described before - his ears purified, nose, tongue, body, and mind-roots all purified.

"After he got them six roots cleaned up like that, his life was extended - extended by two hundred million billion nayutas of years. And he went everywhere teaching this Lotus Sutra to the people.

"Now them four kinds of arrogant folks - them monks and nuns and brothers and sisters who had looked down on him, who had given him that name Never Looked Down - when they seen that he had obtained great supernatural powers, great eloquence in teaching, great power of good stillness, when they heard what he was saying, every one of them came to believe, came to submit, came to follow him.

"And this Bodhisattva went on to convert thousands of myriads of millions of living beings, causing them to dwell in that supreme perfect enlightenment, that anuttara-samyak-sambodhi.

"After his life ended, he met two thousand million Buddhas, all named Sun-Moon-Lamp-Light. In their Dharma, he taught this Lotus Sutra. Because of this cause and condition, he met another two thousand million Buddhas, all named Cloud-Sovereign-Lamp-King. In all these Buddhas' Dharma, he received, held, recited, and taught this sutra to the four kinds of people. And because of this, he got them constantly purified eyes, purified ears, nose, tongue, body, and mind-roots. When he taught the Dharma among them four kinds of people, his heart had no fear at all."

## THE REVELATION - THAT WAS ME

"Great Power, this Bodhisattva Never Looked Down, he made offerings to so many Buddhas like this - respecting them, honoring them, praising them, planting all kinds of good roots. And after that, he met thousands of myriads of millions of Buddhas. And in all them Buddhas' Dharma, he taught this sutra. His merit was accomplished, and he became a Buddha.

"Now Great Power, what do you think? That Bodhisattva Never Looked Down back in them days - you think he was somebody else? That was me. That was my own self.

"If I hadn't received, held, recited, and taught this sutra to others in them past lives, I wouldn't have been able to quickly attain this supreme perfect enlightenment, this anuttara-samyak-sambodhi. Because I received, held, recited, and taught this sutra to people in the presence of them former Buddhas, I was able to quickly attain this supreme perfect enlightenment.

"Now Great Power, them four kinds of people back then - them monks and nuns and brothers and sisters who despised me with angry hearts, who looked down on me - because of that, for two hundred million ages they never met a Buddha, never heard the Dharma, never seen the Sangha. For a thousand ages they suffered great torment in the Avīci Hell, the Hell of No Interruption.

"But when that punishment was done, they met up with that Bodhisattva Never Looked Down again, and he taught them toward that supreme perfect enlightenment.

"Now Great Power, what do you think? Them four kinds of people who constantly looked down on that Bodhisattva back then - you think they was somebody else? Right here in this assembly now, there's five hundred Bodhisattvas like Bhadrapāla and others, five hundred monks like Lion-Moon and others, five hundred lay brothers like Thought-of-Buddha and others - all of them who will never turn back from supreme perfect enlightenment - that's who they are.

"Great Power, you got to know: This Lotus Sutra brings great benefit to all them Bodhisattvas and Mahāsattvas. It can cause them to reach that supreme perfect enlightenment. That's why, after the Tathāgata has passed into extinction, all them Bodhisattvas and Mahāsattvas should constantly receive, hold, recite, explain, and copy out this sutra."

## THE BUDDHA SINGS IT IN VERSE

Then the World-Honored One, wanting to say this teaching one more time, spoke in verse:

In the ancient days there was a Buddha,
Name of King Sound-of-Thunder-and-Glory,
His spirit-wisdom was beyond all measure,
He guided everything that lives -
Gods and humans, dragons and spirits,
All of them made offerings to him.

After that Buddha passed into extinction,
When the Dharma was about to end,
There was one Bodhisattva
Whose name was Never Looked Down.

Now at that time them four kinds of people,
They was holding on tight to doctrines,
Clinging to their understanding of the law.

Never Looked Down Bodhisattva,
He went right up to where they was,
And he spoke these words to them:
"I wouldn't dare look down on you -
All of you are walking the way,
Every one of you gonna become a Buddha."

When the people heard this,
They looked down on him, they cursed him out,
They talked bad about him, reviled his name.

But Never Looked Down Bodhisattva,
He was able to bear it, able to endure.

When his punishment was finished,
When his life was about to end,
He heard this sutra,
And his six roots was purified.

Because of his supernatural powers,
His life was extended and increased.
He taught this sutra again
To all them people far and wide.

All them people who was clinging to doctrines,
Every one of them received teaching
From this Bodhisattva,
Was brought to accomplishment,
Was caused to dwell in the Buddha-way.

When Never Looked Down's life ended,
He met countless Buddhas.
Because he taught this sutra,
He gained immeasurable blessings,
Gradually perfected his merit,
And quickly accomplished the Buddha-way.

That Never Looked Down back then -
That was my own self.

Them four kinds of people at that time,
The ones who was clinging to doctrines,
Who heard Never Looked Down say
"You gonna become a Buddha" -
Because of that cause and condition,
They met countless Buddhas.

These Bodhisattvas in this assembly,
Five hundred of them,
And also them four kinds -
Monks and nuns, believing laymen and laywomen,
The ones now standing before me
Listening to the Dharma - that's who they are.

In my former lives,
I urged all these people
To listen and receive this sutra,
This foremost teaching among teachings.

I opened it up and showed them,
I taught them the way,
I caused them to dwell in nirvāṇa.

Life after life they received and held
A sutra like this one.

For billions and billions of myriads of ages,
So many you can't even think about it,
Only then do you get to hear
This Lotus Sutra.

For billions and billions of myriads of ages,
So many you can't even think about it,
The Buddhas, the World-Honored Ones,
Only once in a while teach this sutra.

Therefore, you practitioners,
After the Buddha has passed into extinction,
When you hear a sutra like this,
Don't let doubt arise in your hearts.

You should with single mind
Teach this sutra far and wide.

Life after life you'll meet Buddhas,
And quickly accomplish the Buddha-way.

### END OF CHAPTER TWENTY: THE BODHISATTVA WHO NEVER LOOKED DOWN

*Blues Interpretation from Classical Chinese by Kumārajīva*

## INTERPRETATION NOTES:

## I. THE BLUES STRUCTURE OF DIGNITY UNDER PERSECUTION

This chapter is pure blues architecture. The Never Looked Down Bodhisattva is the archetypal blues hero - maintaining dignity, faith, and prophetic voice in the face of relentless persecution. The repetitive structure mirrors both the repetition in blues music and the call-and-response tradition:

**The Call**: "I wouldn't dare look down on you. You gonna become a Buddha."
**The Response**: Curses, stones, sticks, mockery.
**The Refrain**: He keeps on saying it anyway. Even from a distance, voice lifted high.

This is the structure of spirituals sung in slavery, of freedom songs sung into police dogs and fire hoses, of gospel truth proclaimed in a world that beats you down. The blues knows how to keep singing when the world wants you silent.

## II. LINGUISTIC CHOICES: VERNACULAR AS THEOLOGICAL STATEMENT

**"Never Looked Down" vs. "Never Disparaging"**

I interpreted 常不輕 (Chang Bu Qing) as "Never Looked Down" rather than the conventional "Never Disparaging" or "Never Despising." This choice does several things:

1. It uses vernacular English that carries the full weight of social hierarchy and oppression - "looking down on somebody" is how systemic degradation is described in African American English
2. It captures the active, ongoing nature of the Chinese 不輕 (bu qing) - "not looking down" is something you DO, a constant practice of seeing people's Buddha-nature
3. It resonates with the blues/gospel tradition of "lifting up" the downtrodden - the opposite of "looking down" is "lifting up," and this Bodhisattva is in the business of lifting up everyone he meets

**"You gonna become a Buddha" - The Prophetic Future Tense**

The repeated proclamation 汝等皆當作佛 (ru deng jie dang zuo fo - "you all will definitely become Buddhas") becomes "You gonna become a Buddha" in blues register. This isn't poor grammar - it's prophetic speech.

The African American prophetic tradition uses "gonna" to declare certain futures against present evidence. "We gonna overcome" sung in jail cells. "You gonna reap what you sow" preached from pulpits. The use of "gonna" here does theological work - it's not speculation, it's declaration. It's faith speaking future transformation into hostile present conditions.

**"Bow down low" - Physical and Spiritual Prostration**

I added "low" to "bow down" (禮拜 - li bai - "prostrate in worship") because in blues/gospel tradition, the depth of the bow matters. "Bow down low" appears in spirituals and gospel songs as the ultimate act of reverence and submission - not to human power, but to divine nature. When Never Looked Down "bows down low" to arrogant monks who will beat him, he's enacting a radical theology: seeing the Buddha-nature beneath the hostile surface and worshiping it even when it's hidden.

This parallels the practice of "making a way out of no way" in Black religious thought - acting on faith in what cannot yet be seen.

**"Lift up his voice high" - Prophetic Proclamation**

When the text says 猶高聲唱言 (you gao sheng chang yan - "still with high voice proclaimed"), I rendered it as "lift up his voice high and call out loud." This is the language of Black preaching, of gospel singing, of prophetic witness. "Lifting up" your voice isn't just volume - it's spiritual elevation, it's making your proclamation heard by heaven even when earth won't listen.

## III. THEOLOGICAL RESONANCES WITH AFRICAN AMERICAN RELIGIOUS TRADITIONS

**The Suffering Servant Who Prophesies to His Persecutors**

Never Looked Down is a suffering servant figure who speaks truth to hostile power. This resonates deeply with African American readings of Isaiah 53, with the figure of Jesus before his accusers, with countless stories of enslaved people maintaining their humanity and prophesying freedom to their enslavers.

The key theological move is: **he sees their Buddha-nature when they cannot see it themselves**. This is what sustained enslaved people - the conviction that their oppressors were spiritually blind, that they themselves could see a truth their masters could not see.

When Never Looked Down says "You gonna become a Buddha" to people beating him with sticks, he's doing what the spirituals did - declaring a future transformation that the present violently denies.

**"Even from a distance" - The Long View of Redemption**

When Never Looked Down runs away from the stones but still calls out from a distance (避走遠住，猶高聲唱言 - "fled to a distance, still with high voice proclaimed"), this captures something essential about the blues perspective on suffering: you can remove yourself from immediate danger while still maintaining your prophetic witness.

This isn't cowardice - it's wisdom. The blues tradition knows when to "fly away" and when to stand and fight. But even in flight, the song continues. Even from a safe distance, the proclamation still rings out.

This is survival strategy and spiritual practice combined. It's what let freedom songs be sung even when singers had to hide. It's the long view that says: I may have to run today, but my words will still reach you, and my prophecy will still come true.

**The Resurrection Through the Word**

The moment when Never Looked Down is dying and suddenly hears all the verses of the Lotus Sutra in the sky (於虛空中，具聞威音王佛、先所說法華經二十千萬億偈，悉能受持) - this is pure gospel. This is the word coming alive at the moment of death. This is resurrection power.

In African American Christian tradition, "the word" has power - spoken, heard, received, it transforms. When Never Looked Down hears the sutra at his death moment and his six roots are purified, his life extended, his power multiplied - this is being "born again," this is resurrection morning, this is the spirit falling on you and making you new.

The parallel to blues/gospel is exact: the song itself has power to transform, to heal, to extend life. When you receive the song deep in your spirit, you become something new.

**The Transformation of Enemies into Disciples**

The revelation that his persecutors suffered in hell but then met him again, and he taught them, and now they're Bodhisattvas in the present assembly (今此會中、跋陀婆羅等五百菩薩) - this is the ultimate blues vision of justice.

It's not revenge. It's not their destruction. It's their transformation. They had to go through hell (literally - Avīci Hell for a thousand ages), but when they came out, he was there waiting to teach them.

This is the deep blues ethic: you don't wish destruction on your oppressor. You prophesy their transformation. You declare that even they, especially they, gonna become Buddha. And when they finally hear it, after all the suffering, after all the resistance, they become your disciples.

This is James Baldwin's "The Fire Next Time": "If we do not now dare everything, the fulfillment of that prophecy, re-created from the Bible in song by a slave, is upon us: God gave Noah the rainbow sign, No more water, the fire next time!"

The prophecy is both warning and promise. You gonna become Buddha - but if you reject it now, you got to go through fire first. Either way, the prophecy stands.

## IV. THE STRUCTURE OF CALL AND RESPONSE

I structured the interpretation to emphasize the call-and-response pattern that's implicit in the Chinese text:

**His call**: "I wouldn't dare look down on you. You gonna become a Buddha."
**Their response**: Curses, stones, sticks.
**His refrain**: "You gonna become a Buddha." (unchanged, undeterred)

This pattern repeats "for many years" (經歷多年) - the Chinese captures duration, persistence. The blues captures the same through repetition, through the refrain that comes back no matter what.

In the verse section, I let this pattern become even more explicit:

Never Looked Down Bodhisattva,
He went right up to where they was,
And he spoke these words to them...

When the people heard this,
They looked down on him, they cursed him out...

But Never Looked Down Bodhisattva,
He was able to bear it, able to endure.

This is how gospel testimonies are structured. This is how freedom songs work. The pattern itself carries meaning - the repetition says "we won't stop," the refrain says "this truth stands."

## V. GRAMMAR AS THEOLOGY: "WAS" VS. "WERE"

I deliberately used vernacular African American English grammar throughout, including constructions like:
- "Where he come from?" (instead of "did he come")
- "them four kinds of people" (instead of "those four kinds")
- "He was able to bear it" (maintaining standard past tense where it serves rhythm)
- "they was clinging" (using "was" with plural subjects where vernacular demands it)

This is not incorrect English. This is a fully systematic dialect with its own grammatical rules, used by millions of native speakers, carrying rich theological and cultural freight.

Using this grammar is making a claim: this wisdom tradition (Buddhism) can speak in this wisdom tradition (African American vernacular). The Dharma can be preached in the language that preached freedom. The Lotus Sutra can be sung in the voice that sang spirituals.

To "correct" this grammar would be to reject the theological work it's doing. It would be to say that certain wisdom must stay in certain linguistic registers. But this interpretation insists: the Buddha-Dharma speaks in every tongue, including this one.
