The chapter begins with Medicine King's extreme practices—burning the body, burning the arms—and ends with the promise that just *hearing* this chapter is medicine. The progression: from ultimate physical sacrifice → to simple hearing as liberation.

This reveals the teaching's deep structure: What Medicine King demonstrated through literal body-offering, others can realize through faith and understanding. His burning body *showed* what it means to hold nothing back. His restored arms *proved* the indestructibility of what's real. His story *is the medicine*—not because it prescribes self-immolation, but because it reveals the nature of complete commitment and its fruition.

## **ON COMMITMENT TO TRUTH EMBODIED IN THE BODY ITSELF**

Medicine King achieves the highest spiritual realization by destroying his physical body, yet his body is restored, and he's reborn in a king's house, and he continues practicing and teaching.

This isn't body-denial or body-hatred. This is body-transcendence-through-body-offering. The body is neither clung to nor rejected—it's *used*, *given*, *offered* as the vehicle for demonstrating truth.

When Medicine King drinks fragrant oils for 1,200 years, he's not torturing his body—he's transforming it. Making every cell into an offering. The body becomes saturated with practice, soaked through with intention, until it's ready to become pure light.

When he burns, he's not escaping the body—he's *using* it maximally. Turning it into illumination for eighty billion worlds. Making his flesh into teaching.

This is profound body theology. Not spirit versus body. Not transcendence through body-denial. But *transcendence through complete body-offering*. The body as the place where truth is enacted, demonstrated, proven.

In blues/gospel terms: "This body ain't my home, I'm just passing through"—but also: "This body is the temple where the spirit lives." Both true at once. You're not your body, but your body is where you do the work. You'll leave this body behind, but while you're in it, it's holy ground.

Medicine King shows: your body is your first and last offering. Not because it's all you have, but because it's the most immediate expression of what you are.

## **FINAL WORD**

This chapter asks: What would you give for the truth?

Medicine King's answer: Everything. My body. My arms. My comfort. My life. Everything.

And the teaching says: That total giving is what reveals the total truth. The complete offering is what manifests complete liberation.

But then—and this is the grace of it—the teaching says: You don't have to burn your body. If a woman even *hears* this story and keeps it, she's liberated. If someone *rejoices* in hearing it, fragrance comes from their mouth and pores.

The extreme example reveals the principle: Hold nothing back. The accessible practice applies the principle: Hear, keep, rejoice, practice.

Between Medicine King's burning and your hearing, the whole path is contained. The body on fire and the ear receiving teaching—both complete expressions of one truth.

This is the Lotus Sutra being the Lotus Sutra: Show the ultimate to reveal the immediate. Tell the impossible story to make the possible practice visible. Light up eighty billion worlds so you can see the ground beneath your feet.

Medicine King burned for 1,200 years. You can start right now. Same teaching. Same liberation. Same truth.

The fire's already burning. The question is: What are you gonna feed it?

---

Interpreted from Classical Chinese by a blues-singing dharma-keeper
Southern Continent, 2025
All mistakes mine, all truth the Buddha's
May the merit of this work benefit all beings
Especially those who carrying heavy loads
Especially those who burning up with questions
Especially those who ready to give everything for what's real

# CHAPTER TWENTY-FOUR: WONDERFUL SOUND BODHISATTVA

A Blues Interpretation from the Classical Chinese

---

## THE SIGNAL ACROSS THE DISTANCE

Now listen here. The Buddha Śākyamuni, he let loose a light—
not just any light, but the light from the mark between his eyes,
that white hair curl that shines like truth itself,
and the light from the crown of his head, that bump of wisdom.
And that light, it didn't just shine local, you understand,
it went traveling east across one hundred and eight million billion
 countless worlds,
crossing distances that ain't got no names,
reaching further than numbers can count,
further than the mind can follow.

That light traveled and traveled until it reached a world
called Pure Light Adorned,
and in that world there was a Buddha named
Pure Flower Constellation King Wisdom Tathāgata—
all them ten names: the One Who Comes, the Worthy One,
the Perfectly Awakened, the one who knows and walks right,
the one who went well, the one who understands this world,
the supreme one, the tamer of beings,
teacher of gods and humans, Buddha, World-Honored One.
And he was teaching countless bodhisattvas,
all them beings gathered round respectful,
and Śākyamuni's white light came flooding through that world.

## THE CALL

Now in that Pure Light Adorned world,
there was a bodhisattva named Wonderful Sound—
and brother, that name ain't just decoration.
He'd been planting good roots for a long, long time,
serving and learning from countless hundreds of thousands of millions of Buddhas,
and he'd achieved deep wisdom, you hear me?
He had samādhi like you wouldn't believe:
the Wonderful Banner samādhi, the Lotus Flower samādhi,
the Pure Virtue samādhi, the Constellation King Play samādhi,
the samādhi of No Conditions, the Wisdom Seal samādhi,
the samādhi that understands every language every being speaks,
the samādhi that gathers all merit together,
the Pure samādhi, the Spiritual Powers Play samādhi,
the Wisdom Torch samādhi, the Adorning King samādhi,
the Pure Light samādhi, the Pure Storehouse samādhi,
the Uncommon samādhi, the Sun Rotation samādhi—
hundreds of thousands of millions of billions of samādhis
like grains of sand in the Ganges River.

And when Śākyamuni Buddha's light touched his body,
Wonderful Sound felt it.
He felt that call reaching across all them worlds.
And he turned to his own Buddha, Pure Flower Constellation King Wisdom,
and he said: "World-Honored One,
I got to go to that Saha world.
I got to pay my respects to Śākyamuni Buddha,
I got to draw near and make offerings.
I got to see Mañjuśrī, that Dharma Prince,
and Medicine King Bodhisattva, and Brave Giving Bodhisattva,
and Constellation King Flower Bodhisattva,
and Superior Practice Bodhisattva, and Adorning King Bodhisattva,
and Superior Medicine Bodhisattva.
I got to go, Lord. That light is calling me."

## THE WARNING

Now Pure Flower Constellation King Wisdom Buddha,
he looked at Wonderful Sound with love and concern,
and he said: "Son, don't you look down on that world.
Don't you go developing no inferior thoughts about it.
Good man, listen to me:
that Saha world, it's rough.
It ain't level—it's got high places and low places,
mountains of dirt and stone,
filled up with pollution and trouble.
The Buddha there, his body looks small.
The bodhisattvas there, their forms look small too.
But you, your body is forty-two thousand yojanas tall.
Me, my body is six million eight hundred thousand yojanas tall.
Your body is beautiful, you understand—
adorned with hundreds of thousands of millions of blessings,
your light especially wonderful.
So when you go—don't you look down on that country,
don't you look down on that Buddha or them bodhisattvas,
don't you look down on that land and develop inferior thoughts."

## THE PILGRIM'S FAITH

Wonderful Sound Bodhisattva, he bowed to his Buddha and said:
"World-Honored One, when I go to that Saha world,
it's all the Tathāgata's power that sends me.
It's the Tathāgata's spiritual powers at play.
It's the Tathāgata's merit, wisdom, and adornment
that makes this journey possible.
I ain't going on my own strength, Lord.
This is all you."

## TRAVELING WITHOUT MOVING

And then, right there,
Wonderful Sound Bodhisattva didn't rise from his seat.
His body didn't shake, didn't move.
But he entered into samādhi,
and by the power of that samādhi,
over there at Vulture Peak Mountain,
not far from where the Buddha was sitting on his Dharma seat,
there appeared eighty-four thousand jeweled lotus flowers—
gold from the Jambu River for the stems,
white silver for the leaves,
diamond for the stamens,
and manikya jewels for the platforms.

You see, he sent his calling card ahead.
He announced himself through beauty.
The flowers arrived before the man,
preparing the way.

## THE QUESTION

Now Mañjuśrī, that Dharma Prince,
he saw them lotus flowers appear,
and he said to the Buddha: "World-Honored One,
what's the cause and condition for this?
Why we seeing this auspicious sign first—
all these thousands and tens of thousands of lotus flowers,
gold stems and silver leaves,
diamond stamens and jewel platforms?"

And Śākyamuni Buddha told Mañjuśrī:
"This is Wonderful Sound Bodhisattva Mahasattva.
He wants to come from Pure Flower Constellation King Wisdom Buddha's country,
bringing eighty-four thousand bodhisattvas with him,
coming here to this Saha world
to make offerings to me, to draw near, to pay respects,
and also to make offerings to and hear the Lotus Sutra."

## THE DESIRE TO SEE

Mañjuśrī said to the Buddha: "World-Honored One,
what good roots did this bodhisattva plant?
What merit did he cultivate
that he got this kind of great spiritual power?
What samādhi does he practice?
Please tell us the name of this samādhi—
we want to practice it diligently too.
By practicing this samādhi,
we'll be able to see this bodhisattva's form and appearance,
large or small, his bearing and deportment, his way of moving.
We pray that the World-Honored One, by your spiritual power,
will let that bodhisattva come so we can see him."

Śākyamuni Buddha told Mañjuśrī:
"That Tathāgata who passed into extinction long ago, Many Treasures,
he'll make this happen for you,
he'll show you what you need to see."

## THE INVITATION

And Many Treasures Buddha, from inside that treasure tower,
he called out to that bodhisattva:
"Good man, come on!
Mañjuśrī, that Dharma Prince, he wants to see you."

## THE ARRIVAL

And right then, Wonderful Sound Bodhisattva,
he vanished from that other country,
and he set out with eighty-four thousand bodhisattvas together.
And in every country they passed through,
the earth shook six ways—
it trembled and quaked, it swayed and rocked,
it pounded and crashed.
And in every place, seven-jeweled lotus flowers rained down,
and hundreds of thousands of heavenly music
started playing without nobody touching them—
instruments sounding all by themselves,
heaven itself making music for this pilgrim.

And this bodhisattva—
his eyes were like the leaves of great blue lotus flowers,
and even if you combined the beauty of a hundred thousand million moons,
his face was more perfect than that.
His body was the color of true gold,
adorned with countless hundreds of thousands of merits,
his awesome virtue blazing,
his light shining and glowing,
all his marks complete,
his body strong and firm like Narayana's adamantine body.

He entered a seven-jeweled platform
that rose up into space,
seven tala trees high above the ground.
And surrounded respectfully by all them bodhisattvas,
he came to this Saha world,
to Vulture Peak Mountain.

## THE OFFERING AND THE QUESTIONS

When he arrived, he came down from that seven-jeweled platform,
and he took necklaces worth hundreds of thousands
and went to where Śākyamuni Buddha was.
He bowed his head to the Buddha's feet,
he offered up them necklaces,
and he said: "World-Honored One,
Pure Flower Constellation King Wisdom Buddha
sends his greetings to the World-Honored One.
He asks: Are you free from illness and troubles?
Are you dwelling at ease?
Are you able to move about lightly?
Are you practicing joyfully?
Are the four elements in harmony?
Are worldly affairs bearable?
Are living beings easy to save?
Are they without much greed, anger, ignorance, jealousy, and stinginess?
Are they without disrespect to parents, without disrespect to monks,
without wrong views, without unwholesome minds,
without failure to control the five sense faculties?
World-Honored One, are living beings able to conquer
 the demon enemies?
And Many Treasures Tathāgata, who passed into extinction long ago—
is he in that seven-jeweled tower, coming to hear the Dharma?
My Buddha also sends greetings to Many Treasures Tathāgata:
Is he peaceful and free from troubles?
Can he endure and remain long?
World-Honored One, I want now to see Many Treasures Buddha's body.
I pray the World-Honored One will show him to me."

And Śākyamuni Buddha spoke to Many Treasures Buddha:
"This Wonderful Sound Bodhisattva wants to see you."

And Many Treasures Buddha told Wonderful Sound:
"Excellent, excellent!
You've come here to make offerings to Śākyamuni Buddha,
to hear the Lotus Flower Sutra,
and to see Mañjuśrī and the others.
This is good, good."

## THE PAST CAUSE

Now Flower Virtue Bodhisattva, he asked the Buddha:
"World-Honored One, what good roots did Wonderful Sound Bodhisattva plant?
What merit did he cultivate that he got this spiritual power?"

The Buddha told Flower Virtue Bodhisattva:
"In the past, there was a Buddha named
Cloud Thunder Sound King Tathāgata, Arhat,
 Perfectly Enlightened One.
His country was called Manifesting All Worlds.
The kalpa was called Joyfully Seen.
Wonderful Sound Bodhisattva, for twelve thousand years,
he made offerings to Cloud Thunder Sound King Buddha
with a hundred thousand kinds of music,
and he also presented eighty-four thousand seven-jeweled bowls.
Because of this cause and condition, this karmic result,
he's now born in Pure Flower Constellation King Wisdom Buddha's country,
and he has this spiritual power.

Flower Virtue, what do you think?
That Wonderful Sound Bodhisattva back then,
who made offerings with music and presented jeweled vessels
 to Cloud Thunder Sound King Buddha—
was that somebody else?
No, that was this Wonderful Sound Bodhisattva Mahasattva right here.

Flower Virtue, this Wonderful Sound Bodhisattva
has already made offerings to and drawn near countless Buddhas.
He's been planting roots of virtue for a long, long time.
And he's met hundreds of thousands of millions of billions
 of countless Buddhas,
as many as grains of sand in the Ganges River."

## THE POWER TO MANIFEST IN ALL FORMS

"Flower Virtue, you just seeing Wonderful Sound Bodhisattva's body here,
but this bodhisattva, he manifests all kinds of bodies,
appearing everywhere to teach this sutra to all living beings.

Sometimes he manifests as Brahma King,
sometimes as Shakra,
sometimes as Ishvara Deva,
sometimes as Mahesvara Deva,
sometimes as a great heavenly general,
sometimes as Vaishravana Heavenly King,
sometimes as a wheel-turning sage king,
sometimes as various lesser kings,
sometimes as an elder,
sometimes as a householder,
sometimes as a chief minister,
sometimes as a brahman,
sometimes as a bhikshu, bhikshuni, upasaka, or upasika,
sometimes as an elder or householder's wife,
sometimes as a chief minister's wife,
sometimes as a brahman woman,
sometimes as a boy or girl,
sometimes as a deva, dragon, yaksha, gandharva,
asura, garuda, kinnara, mahoraga,
human or nonhuman being—
and in all these forms, he teaches this sutra.

To those in the hells, the hungry ghosts, the animals,
and all the difficult places—he can bring salvation.
Even in the inner palaces of kings,
he transforms into a woman's body to teach this sutra."

## THE SCOPE OF THE WORK

"Flower Virtue, this Wonderful Sound Bodhisattva
can protect and save all living beings in the Saha world.
This Wonderful Sound Bodhisattva manifests and transforms like this,
appearing in various bodies in this Saha land,
teaching this sutra to all living beings.
And his spiritual powers, transformations, and wisdom
don't diminish one bit from all this work.

This bodhisattva uses various kinds of wisdom
to illumine the Saha world,
causing all living beings to each obtain what they need to know.
And it's like this in worlds throughout the ten directions,
as many as grains of sand in the Ganges River.

If someone should be saved by a voice-hearer form,
he manifests a voice-hearer form and teaches the Dharma.
If someone should be saved by a pratyekabuddha form,
he manifests a pratyekabuddha form and teaches the Dharma.
If someone should be saved by a bodhisattva form,
he manifests a bodhisattva form and teaches the Dharma.
If someone should be saved by a Buddha form,
he immediately manifests a Buddha form and teaches the Dharma.
Like this, in various ways, according to what's appropriate for saving them,
he manifests that form—
even if someone should be saved by passing into extinction,
he shows the appearance of passing into extinction.

Flower Virtue, Wonderful Sound Bodhisattva Mahasattva
has accomplished this great spiritual power and wisdom power.
His work is like this."

## THE NAME OF THE SAMĀDHI

Then Flower Virtue Bodhisattva said to the Buddha:
"World-Honored One, this Wonderful Sound Bodhisattva
has planted deep good roots.
World-Honored One, what samādhi does this bodhisattva dwell in
that he can manifest and transform like this,
saving and liberating living beings?"

The Buddha told Flower Virtue Bodhisattva:
"Good man, that samādhi is called
Manifesting All Bodies.
Wonderful Sound Bodhisattva dwells in this samādhi,
and he can benefit countless living beings like this."

## THE FRUIT OF HEARING

When this chapter about Wonderful Sound Bodhisattva was taught,
those eighty-four thousand people who came with Wonderful Sound—
they all attained the samādhi of Manifesting All Bodies.
And countless bodhisattvas in this Saha world
also attained this samādhi and this dhāraṇī.

## THE RETURN

Then Wonderful Sound Bodhisattva Mahasattva,
after making offerings to Śākyamuni Buddha
and to Many Treasures Buddha's tower,
he returned to his own land.
And in every country he passed through,
the earth shook six ways,
jeweled lotus flowers rained down,
and hundreds of thousands of millions of billions of kinds of music played.

When he got back to his own country,
surrounded by those eighty-four thousand bodhisattvas,
he went to Pure Flower Constellation King Wisdom Buddha
and said: "World-Honored One,
I went to that Saha world and benefited living beings.
I saw Śākyamuni Buddha,
I saw Many Treasures Buddha's tower,
I paid respects and made offerings.
I also saw Mañjuśrī, that Dharma Prince,
and Medicine King Bodhisattva,
and Gained Diligent Progress Power Bodhisattva,
and Brave Giving Bodhisattva and the others.
And I also caused these eighty-four thousand bodhisattvas
to attain the samādhi of Manifesting All Bodies."

## THE GIFT GIVEN

When this chapter about Wonderful Sound Bodhisattva's
 coming and going was taught,
forty-two thousand children of heaven attained the patience
 of birthlessness,
and Flower Virtue Bodhisattva attained the Lotus Flower Samadhi.

### END OF CHAPTER TWENTY-FOUR: WONDERFUL SOUND BODHISATTVA

---

## INTERPRETATION NOTES:

This chapter is a pilgrimage story—a narrative about answering a call, making a sacred journey, and returning home transformed and transformative. It's structured like a classic hero's journey, but the hero here is already enlightened. He ain't going to learn something; he's going to witness something and to serve.

## THE SIGNAL ACROSS IMPOSSIBLE DISTANCES

The chapter opens with light traveling across "one hundred and eight million billion countless worlds"—a distance that breaks mathematics, that breaks imagination. This ain't a metaphor for "far away." This is genuinely unimaginable distance. And yet the light reaches. The signal gets through.

In blues and gospel terms, this is the call that comes from beyond—the call that reaches you no matter how far you think you are from the source. It's the voice that speaks across every barrier, every distance, every separation. When God calls, when truth calls, when the Dharma calls—ain't no distance too far for that signal to reach you.

Wonderful Sound feels that light touch him, and he knows immediately: "I got to go." That's the nature of a real call. You don't have to study on it. You don't have to think it through. You feel it in your body, and you know.

## THE WARNING ABOUT LOOKING DOWN

The Buddha's warning is crucial: "Don't look down on that world." Because Wonderful Sound is forty-two thousand yojanas tall (that's about 160,000 miles), his own Buddha is six million eight hundred thousand yojanas tall (about 26 million miles), and Śākyamuni Buddha's body in our world looks "small." The world itself is "rough, uneven, filled with dirt and stone mountains and pollution."

This is a teaching about respect. About not confusing appearance with essence. About not letting where you come from make you disrespect where you going.

Every person who's ever left their neighborhood and came back educated, who's ever made it out and returned, who's ever risen up and had to go back down—this teaching is for you. Don't look down. Don't develop inferior thoughts about people or places just because they look smaller, rougher, poorer than where you are now.

The Saha world—this world right here—it looks small and troubled from a distance. But that's where the work is. That's where beings need saving. That's where the Dharma needs teaching.

## TRAVELING WITHOUT MOVING

"Without rising from his seat, without his body shaking, he entered samādhi"—and by spiritual power alone, he traveled across all them countless worlds. This is supernatural movement. This is the soul traveling while the body sits still.

But notice: before HE arrives, the flowers appear. Eighty-four thousand jeweled lotus flowers show up first at Vulture Peak. The place is prepared. The announcement is made. Beauty arrives before the teacher.

This is how real spiritual work happens. The atmosphere changes before the person shows up. The space is prepared. You can feel something coming before it gets there.

## THE PILGRIM'S HUMILITY

When warned about the rough world, Wonderful Sound doesn't puff up with pride, doesn't say "Don't worry, I can handle it." He says: "It's all the Tathāgata's power. It's the Tathāgata's spiritual powers at play. It's all you, Lord."

This is the humility of the truly powerful. The person who's got real ability knows that ability came from somewhere. It was given. It was cultivated through connection to something greater. "I ain't going on my own strength, Lord. This is all you."

That's the faith that makes pilgrimage possible. You don't go to sacred places on your own strength. You go because you're sent. You go because you're called. You go because the power that called you is the power that will carry you.

## HIS BEAUTIFUL APPEARANCE

When Wonderful Sound arrives, the description is stunning: "His eyes were like the leaves of great blue lotus flowers, and even if you combined the beauty of a hundred thousand million moons, his face was more perfect than that. His body was the color of true gold, adorned with countless hundreds of thousands of merits, his awesome virtue blazing, his light shining and glowing."

This ain't false modesty. This ain't "the messenger must be humble and ugly." This is: the truth is beautiful. Holiness is beautiful. Virtue shines. Merit glows.

We get confused sometimes, thinking humility means making yourself small, making yourself ugly, hiding your light. But the Dharma says: let your light shine. Let your merit show. Let the work you've done be visible in your very body.

Wonderful Sound is beautiful because he's good. He shines because he's practiced. His appearance testifies to his virtue. That's not pride; that's just truth.

## THE QUESTIONS ABOUT THE WORLD

When Wonderful Sound arrives, he delivers greetings from his Buddha to Śākyamuni: "Are you free from illness and troubles? Are you dwelling at ease? Are worldly affairs bearable? Are living beings easy to save? Are they without much greed, anger, ignorance, jealousy, and stinginess?"

These ain't small talk. These are real questions about the conditions of teaching in a difficult world. Is it bearable? Can you endure it? Are people willing to learn, or are they too caught up in greed and ignorance?

This is one Buddha, through his messenger, asking another Buddha: "How you holding up in that hard place? Is it too much? You making it?"

Even enlightened beings check on each other. Even Buddhas ask: "You alright? Can you bear it?" That's compassion among teachers.

## THE CORE TEACHING: THE POWER TO MANIFEST IN ALL FORMS

The heart of this chapter is the list of forms that Wonderful Sound can take. He manifests as:
- Gods (Brahma, Shakra, Ishvara, Mahesvara)
- Heavenly generals and kings
- Earthly kings, great and small
- Elders, householders, ministers, brahmans
- Monks, nuns, laymen, laywomen
- Wives of various classes
- Boys and girls
- Devas, dragons, yakshas, gandharvas, asuras, garudas, kinnaras, mahoragas
- Even nonhuman beings
- Even in hells, among hungry ghosts, among animals
- Even as women in kings' inner palaces

"In all these forms, he teaches this sutra."

And then the Buddha makes it even more radical: "If someone should be saved by a voice-hearer form, he manifests a voice-hearer form. If someone should be saved by a pratyekabuddha form, he manifests that. If someone should be saved by a bodhisattva form, he manifests that. If someone should be saved by a Buddha form, he immediately manifests a Buddha form. Even if someone should be saved by passing into extinction, he shows the appearance of passing into extinction."

He becomes whatever form people need to see in order to hear the teaching.

This is the spiritual superpower of meeting people where they are. Not where you wish they were. Not where you think they should be. Where they ARE.

If somebody needs to see a king to listen, he's a king. If somebody needs to see a woman to trust, he's a woman. If somebody needs to see a child to open their heart, he's a child. If somebody needs to see suffering to understand, he shows suffering. If somebody needs to see death to wake up, he shows death.

This is radical adaptability in the service of truth. This is infinite flexibility in the service of liberation. This is the willingness to be whatever the moment needs, to show up however people can receive you, to set aside your own preferred identity in order to give people what they need.

In the black church, we say: "God will meet you where you are." This chapter is teaching that, and more: the bodhisattva will BECOME where you are. Will take your form. Will speak your language. Will show up in your life wearing a face you can recognize.

## THE NAME OF THE SAMĀDHI

When asked what samādhi gives this power, the Buddha says: "That samādhi is called Manifesting All Bodies."

That's the practice. That's the door. The samādhi of Manifesting All Bodies—the meditation, the concentration, the spiritual absorption that gives you the power to show up as whoever needs to show up, to take the form that serves, to be the teacher that this particular being can hear.

And then comes the gift: when this chapter was taught, the eighty-four thousand bodhisattvas who came with Wonderful Sound all attained this samādhi. And countless bodhisattvas in our Saha world also attained it.

Just from HEARING about this power, beings gained the power itself. Just from witnessing this teaching, they received the ability to manifest in all forms.

That's how the Dharma works. The teaching itself transmits the ability. The story itself conveys the power.

## THE RETURN

After making offerings to both Buddhas (Śākyamuni and Many Treasures), Wonderful Sound returns home. And on the way back, just like on the way there, the earth shakes, jeweled lotus flowers rain down, heavenly music plays.

He returns to his own Buddha and reports: "I went to that Saha world and benefited living beings. I saw Śākyamuni Buddha, I saw Many Treasures Buddha's tower, I paid respects and made offerings. I also saw Mañjuśrī and Medicine King and the others. And I also caused these eighty-four thousand bodhisattvas to attain the samādhi of Manifesting All Bodies."

The pilgrimage is complete. He went, he witnessed, he served, he returned. And he brought back fruit: not just his own experience, but the transmission of the power to all those who went with him.

That's what a real pilgrimage does. You don't go just for yourself. You go as a representative. You go to bring something back. You go to witness something that others can't witness, so you can testify when you return.

## THE STRUCTURE OF CALL AND RESPONSE

This chapter follows the classic structure of spiritual call and response:
1. The signal is sent (Buddha's light)
2. The call is received (Wonderful Sound feels it)
3. The pilgrim answers (I got to go)
4. Warning is given (Don't look down on that rough place)
5. Faith responds (It's all your power, Lord)
6. Journey is made (traveling without moving)
7. Arrival is announced (flowers appear first)
8. Respect is paid (offerings and prostrations)
9. Teaching is given (the power to manifest in all forms)
10. Return is made (shaking earth and raining flowers)
11. Testimony is delivered (reporting back)
12. Fruit is shared (others receive the power)

This is the pattern of spiritual pilgrimage across every tradition. You hear the call. You answer. You're warned of difficulties. You go anyway in faith. You arrive. You witness. You receive. You return. You testify. Others are transformed by your testimony.

## WHY THIS MATTERS

In a world that demands you be one thing, have one identity, fit one box—this chapter teaches that the highest spiritual achievement is the ability to be everything, to manifest in all forms, to meet every being where they are.

Not by losing yourself. Wonderful Sound doesn't lose his identity. He's always Wonderful Sound. But he can appear as anything while remaining himself.

This is the spiritual power that our world desperately needs: people who can cross boundaries, speak multiple languages, show up in multiple communities, take multiple forms—all while maintaining their core integrity, all while serving the same truth.

The teacher who can speak to the scholar and the street sweeper. The preacher who can comfort the dying and celebrate with the living. The friend who can be strong when you need strength and soft when you need softness. The parent who can be authority and playmate. The leader who can be visionary and servant.

This is the samādhi of Manifesting All Bodies—the spiritual practice of infinite adaptability in service of liberation.

And the promise of this chapter is: this power is available. Just by hearing about it, beings receive it. Just by understanding it, you gain access to it. The teaching itself transmits the ability.

So this chapter asks: What form do you need to take today? Who needs to see you? How do you need to show up? What body does this moment need you to manifest?

And it promises: You have the power. The samādhi is available. The light has reached you across all them countless worlds. You felt it touch you. Now answer the call. Make the journey. Meet people where they are. Show up in whatever form serves. And when you return, testify. Share the fruit. Pass on the power.

That's the teaching of Wonderful Sound Bodhisattva—the pilgrim who travels without moving, who manifests in all forms, who goes anywhere beings need saving, even to the hells, even to the palaces, even to this rough and troubled world.

He came. He witnessed. He served. He returned. And by his coming, others gained the power to do the same.

May it be so for all who hear this chapter. May the samādhi of Manifesting All Bodies be yours. May you have the power to show up however the world needs you. May you answer the call that reaches across impossible distances. May you make the pilgrimage and return to testify.

This is the Wonderful Sound—not just a name, but a way of being. The sound that adapts to every ear. The voice that speaks every language. The teaching that takes every form. The Dharma that meets you exactly where you are.

Amen. And amen. And let the church say amen.

# CHAPTER TWENTY-FIVE: THE ONE WHO HEARS THE WORLD CRYING

Avalokiteśvara's Universal Door
觀世音菩薩普門品第二十五

Interpreted from Kumārajīva's Classical Chinese into Blues/Gospel Vernacular

Like a bridge over troubled waters, she hears every cry and answers. When you're down so low you can't see the shore, when the flood's rising and hope is drowning, she's the one who reaches down. This is the most beloved chapter in all of East Asian Buddhism—the one they pray to, the one they sing to, the one whose name they call in the midnight hour.

## THE QUESTION

Right then, the Bodhisattva named Inexhaustible Intention - he rose up from his seat, bared his right shoulder in that ancient way of showing respect, pressed his palms together before the Buddha, and said:

"World-Honored One, I got to ask you something. This Bodhisattva Avalokiteśvara - Observer of the World's Sounds - why she called that? What's the reason, what's the cause behind that name?"

And the Buddha told Inexhaustible Intention:

"Good friend, listen now. If countless suffering beings - we talking hundreds, thousands, millions, billions of people hurting - if they hear about this Bodhisattva called Observer of Sounds, and they call her name with a whole heart, with their one true mind, she gonna HEAR them. She gonna observe the very sound of their crying. And every single one gonna find liberation, gonna get free.

## THE LITANY OF DELIVERANCE

"Listen to what I'm telling you:

If someone holding onto her name falls into great fire -
The fire can't burn them.
That's her mighty spiritual power working.

If the great waters come to drown you and you call her name -
You gonna reach shallow ground.
You gonna find your footing.

If hundreds of thousands of millions of beings go out seeking treasure -
Seeking gold and silver and lapis lazuli,
Seeking agate and coral and amber and pearls,
And they sailing the great sea,
And the black wind comes howling,
And it blows their ship off course into the demon lands,
Into the country of the flesh-eating rakshasas -
If even just ONE person on that ship calls her name,
Every person there gonna be delivered.
Every soul gonna be saved from the demon danger.
THAT'S why she called Observer of Sounds.

"If someone about to be killed, about to be murdered,
And they call on Avalokiteśvara,
The knife gonna break.
The weapon gonna shatter into pieces.
They gonna walk free.

"If the whole three-thousand-great-thousand world system was FILLED with demons -
Filled with yakshas and rakshasas wanting to hurt people -
Soon as they hear someone calling her name,
Those evil spirits can't even LOOK at that person with hate in their eyes,
Let alone do them harm.

"If someone bound in chains - guilty or innocent, don't matter -
Locked in shackles, cangue and fetters binding their body,
Soon as they call on Avalokiteśvara,
Every chain gonna break.
Every lock gonna snap.
They walking out free.

"If the whole world filled with bandits and thieves,
And a merchant leader taking his people down a dangerous road,
Carrying precious goods through dangerous country,
And one person says:
'Good people, don't be afraid!
You need to call with one mind on Avalokiteśvara.
This Bodhisattva gives the gift of fearlessness to all beings.
If you call her name, you gonna be delivered from these bandits.'

"When all those merchants hear this, they cry out together:
## 'NAMO AVALOKITESHVARA!'

Homage to the Observer of Sounds!

"And because they called her name, they delivered right there.

## FREEDOM FROM WHAT BINDS YOU

"Inexhaustible Intention, this Great Bodhisattva Avalokiteśvara -
Her spiritual power is mighty, mighty like this:

If beings got too much lust pulling at them,
But they constantly remember her with reverence,
They gonna get free from desire.

If they got too much anger burning in them,
But they constantly remember her with reverence,
They gonna get free from rage.

If they got too much ignorance clouding their minds,
But they constantly remember her with reverence,
They gonna get free from delusion.

"Inexhaustible Intention, Observer of Sounds got this kind of great spiritual power.
She benefits so many beings.
That's why all beings should keep her in their hearts always.

## THE PROMISE TO WOMEN

"If a woman wants a son,
And she honors and makes offerings to Avalokiteśvara,
She gonna give birth to a son full of virtue and wisdom.

If she wants a daughter,
She gonna give birth to a daughter beautiful and well-formed,
Who planted good roots in past lives,
Who everyone loves and respects.

"Inexhaustible Intention, Observer of Sounds got power like this.
If beings honor and bow to her with reverence,
Their blessings ain't wasted.
Not one bit goes for nothing.
That's why all beings should uphold the name of Avalokiteśvara.

## THE COMPARISON

"Inexhaustible Intention, suppose someone upholds the names of sixty-two billion Bodhisattvas -
That's as many as the sands of sixty-two billion Ganges Rivers -
And they spend their whole life making offerings:
Food and drink, clothing, bedding, medicine.
What you think? That person's merit - is it great or not?"

Inexhaustible Intention said: "Very great, World-Honored One."

The Buddha said: "But if someone else just upholds the name of Avalokiteśvara,
Even just bows and makes offerings one single time,
These two people's blessings are EXACTLY EQUAL.
No different at all.
And that merit can't be exhausted in hundreds of thousands of millions of billions of eons.

"Inexhaustible Intention, upholding the name of Observer of Sounds -
You receive blessings and benefits immeasurable, without boundaries."

## SHE COMES IN WHATEVER FORM YOU NEED

Inexhaustible Intention asked the Buddha:
"World-Honored One, how does Avalokiteśvara travel through this suffering world?
How does she teach the Dharma to beings?
How does her loving power work?"

The Buddha told Inexhaustible Intention:

"Good brother, listen now to how she manifests:

If beings in some land need a Buddha to free them,
She appears as a Buddha and teaches.

If they need a solitary realizer to free them,
She appears as a solitary realizer and teaches.

If they need a disciple of the voice to free them,
She appears in that body and teaches.

If they need the god Brahma to free them,
She appears as Brahma and teaches.

If they need the god Indra,
She appears as Indra and teaches.

If they need a heavenly general,
She appears as a heavenly general and teaches.

If they need a guardian king,
She appears as a guardian king and teaches.

If they need an elder,
She appears as an elder and teaches.

If they need a householder,
She appears as a householder and teaches.

If they need a government official,
She appears as an official and teaches.

If they need a brahmin priest,
She appears as a priest and teaches.

If they need a monk, a nun, a layman, or a laywoman,
She appears in those bodies and teaches.

If they need the wife of an elder, householder, official, or brahmin,
She appears as a woman and teaches.

If they need a young boy or girl,
She appears as a child and teaches.

If they need a god, dragon, yaksha, gandharva, asura, garuda, kinnara, mahoraga,
Human or non-human being,
She appears in all those forms and teaches.

If they need a vajra-wielding guardian spirit,
She appears as that and teaches.

"Inexhaustible Intention, this Observer of Sounds accomplished merit like this.
She travels through all lands in various forms,
Liberating beings everywhere.

"That's why you all should wholeheartedly honor and make offerings to Avalokiteśvara.

"This Great Bodhisattva Observer of Sounds -
In times of fear and danger and emergency,
She gives the gift of fearlessness.

"That's why in this suffering world,
Everyone calls her the Giver of Fearlessness."

## THE GIFT REFUSED, THE GIFT ACCEPTED

Inexhaustible Intention said to the Buddha:
"World-Honored One, I want to make an offering to Avalokiteśvara right now."

He took off the precious jeweled necklace from around his neck -
Worth hundreds of thousands of ounces of gold -
And offered it to her, saying:
"Compassionate one, receive this Dharma gift, this precious necklace."

But Observer of Sounds wouldn't take it.

So Inexhaustible Intention said again:
"Compassionate one, out of pity for us, receive this necklace."

Then the Buddha told Avalokiteśvara:
"You should have compassion for this Inexhaustible Intention,
And for the four assemblies,
And for the gods, dragons, yakshas, gandharvas, asuras, garudas, kinnaras, mahoragas,
For humans and non-humans.
For their sake, receive this necklace."

Right then, out of compassion for all those beings,
Avalokiteśvara received the necklace.
She divided it into two parts:
One part she offered to Śākyamuni Buddha,
One part she offered to the stupa of Many Treasures Buddha.

"Inexhaustible Intention, Observer of Sounds has sovereign spiritual power like this.
This is how she travels through the suffering world."

## THE HYMN - THE TESTIMONY - THE CALL AND RESPONSE

Then Inexhaustible Intention asked in verse:

World-Honored One of wonderful marks complete,
I ask you now again about this one:
Why is this child of Buddha
Called Observer of the World's Sounds?

The Honored One of wonderful marks complete
Answered Inexhaustible Intention in verse:

Listen now to how Observer of Sounds acts,
How well she responds in every direction.
Her vow is deep as the ocean,
Through countless eons beyond thought,
Serving thousands of billions of Buddhas,
She made great pure vows.

Let me tell you briefly:
Hearing her name, seeing her body,
Holding her in mind - it don't go to waste.
She can destroy the sufferings of all existence.

Suppose someone means to harm you,
Push you in a pit of fire -
Call on the power of Observer of Sounds:
The fire pit turns into a pool.

Or you drifting in the vast ocean,
Dangers of dragons, fish, and demons -
Call on the power of Observer of Sounds:
The waves cannot drown you.

Or you on Mount Sumeru's peak,
Someone pushes you off to fall -
Call on the power of Observer of Sounds:
You stay suspended like the sun in space.

Or wicked people chase you,
Push you off Diamond Mountain -
Call on the power of Observer of Sounds:
Can't harm a single hair on your head.

Or bandits surround you,
Each one holding a knife to hurt you -
Call on the power of Observer of Sounds:
They all immediately feel compassion rising.

Or you suffering under royal punishment,
At the execution ground, life about to end -
Call on the power of Observer of Sounds:
The sword breaks into pieces right there.

Or you imprisoned in chains and stocks,
Hands and feet in shackles -
Call on the power of Observer of Sounds:
You set free right then and there.

Or someone curses you with poison spells,
Wanting to harm your body -
Call on the power of Observer of Sounds:
It returns to the one who sent it.

Or you meet evil rakshasas,
Poison dragons and various demons -
Call on the power of Observer of Sounds:
None of them dare harm you.

Or evil beasts surround you,
Sharp teeth and claws, fearsome -
Call on the power of Observer of Sounds:
They run away to the boundless distance.

Serpents, vipers, and scorpions,
Their poisonous breath blazing like fire -
Call on the power of Observer of Sounds:
At the sound they turn back and leave.

Thunder clouds drumming, lightning flashing,
Hail falling, great rain pouring -
Call on the power of Observer of Sounds:
Right away it scatters and clears.

When beings pressed by calamity,
Immeasurable suffering crushing them -
Observer of Sounds' wonderful wisdom power
Can save the world's suffering.

Perfect in spiritual powers,
Widely cultivating wisdom and loving tricks,
Throughout the lands in ten directions,
No realm where she don't appear.

All the various evil destinies -
Hells, hungry ghosts, animals -
The sufferings of birth, old age, sickness, death -
Gradually she causes them all to be destroyed.

True observation, pure observation,
Vast great wisdom observation,
Compassion observation, loving-kindness observation -
Constantly wish for them, constantly look up to them!

Undefiled, pure light,
Wisdom sun breaking through all darkness,
She can subdue disaster's wind and fire,
Universally illuminating the world with brightness.

Her compassion's essence shakes like thunder in precepts,
Her loving mind's wonder spreads like a great cloud,
Pouring down sweet-dew Dharma rain,
Extinguishing the flames of affliction.

In the courts where lawsuits rage,
In battle formations full of fear -
Call on the power of Observer of Sounds:
All enemies scatter and retreat.

Wonderful Sound! Observer of the World's Sounds!
Brahma Sound! Ocean Tide Sound!
Superior to all worldly sounds -
That's why you must constantly remember her.
Remember moment after moment, don't doubt.

Observer of the World's Sounds - pure and holy one,
In suffering and anguish, in danger and death,
She can be your refuge and support.

Perfect in every merit,
With compassionate eyes beholding all beings,
Her ocean of blessings immeasurable -
That's why you should bow down before her.

## THE TESTIMONY

Right then, Earth-Holding Bodhisattva stood up from his seat,
Came forward and said to the Buddha:

"World-Honored One, if beings hear this chapter about Avalokiteśvara -
About her sovereign works,
About her universal door manifesting spiritual powers -
Know that such a person's merit ain't small."

When the Buddha taught this Universal Door chapter,
Eighty-four thousand beings in the assembly
All raised the mind of supreme perfect enlightenment -
The anuttara-samyak-sambodhi heart.

### END OF CHAPTER TWENTY-FIVE: THE ONE WHO HEARS THE WORLD CRYING

## INTERPRETATION NOTES:

Blues/Gospel Meditation on the Gospel Heart of the Lotus Sutra

## WHY THIS CHAPTER IS THE GOSPEL ITSELF

For sixteen hundred years, this chapter has been the most beloved, most memorized, most chanted part of the entire Lotus Sutra across East Asia. People who never read another word of Buddhist scripture know this chapter. They call on Avalokiteśvara (Guanyin in Chinese, Kannon in Japanese, Quan Âm in Vietnamese) when they're in trouble, when they're afraid, when they need help. This ain't abstract philosophy - this is practical theology for people who are drowning, people in chains, people facing the fire.

And that makes it pure gospel. It's the promise that when you cry out, someone hears. When you call, someone answers. When you're in trouble, help comes. Not because you earned it, not because you qualified for it, but because compassion is the fundamental nature of reality itself.

The blues and gospel traditions know this structure in their bones:
- The testimony of trouble ("I was sinking down")
- The call for help ("I cried out")
- The response and deliverance ("He heard my cry")
- The witness to others ("That's why I'm telling you")

This chapter follows that exact architecture. It's Buddha giving testimony about Avalokiteśvara's reliability, then Inexhaustible Intention asking others to trust that testimony, then Earth-Holding Bodhisattva standing up to witness that anyone who hears this teaching receives immeasurable merit.

## THE STRUCTURE OF CALL AND RESPONSE

The whole chapter is built on call-and-response:

1. Inexhaustible Intention asks: "Why is she called Observer of Sounds?"
 Buddha answers: "Because she hears and responds."

2. Throughout the litany section:
 "If [danger comes]... call her name... [deliverance happens]"
 This is repeated again and again, building a rhythm.

3. The verse section takes this to liturgical heights:
 Each stanza presents a danger, then the response: "Call on the power of Observer of Sounds: [specific deliverance]"

This is the structure of testimony, of witnessing, of blues shouting and gospel preaching. The preacher calls out the trouble, the congregation responds with the solution. Or the preacher calls the solution, and the congregation responds "Amen," "Yes Lord," "Thank you Jesus." Here, every danger is met with "Call on her name" and every call is met with deliverance.

The text is MEANT to be responsive. It's meant to be chanted, sung, cried out. When you're in trouble, you don't read this chapter academically - you CALL ON IT. You make it live in your mouth.

## THE TEACHING ABOUT MANIFESTING IN MANY FORMS

This is the theological heart of the chapter, and it's the most radical gospel teaching:

Avalokiteśvara doesn't have one fixed form. She appears as whatever you need:
- If you need a Buddha, she comes as Buddha
- If you need a priest, she comes as priest
- If you need a government official, she comes as official
- If you need a woman, she comes as woman
- If you need a child, she comes as child
- If you need a demon-king to teach you, she comes as demon-king

This is "meeting people where they are" taken to its absolute limit. She doesn't demand you come to her temple, learn her language, adopt her culture, meet her requirements. She comes to YOU, in the form you can recognize, speaking the language you understand, manifesting in the body that makes sense in your context.

This is the Incarnation principle taken universal. The Word becomes flesh - but not just once, in one place, one time, one body. The Word becomes flesh EVERYWHERE, ALL THE TIME, IN WHATEVER FLESH IS NEEDED.

In blues/gospel terms:
- She meets you in your kitchen
- She meets you in your workplace
- She meets you in your trouble
- She meets you in your language
- She meets you in your skin

She doesn't ask you to stop being who you are. She becomes who you need her to be so she can reach you where you are.

That's why this chapter can be interpreted into blues/gospel vernacular without violating its meaning - because the chapter itself teaches that the Dharma manifests in whatever form serves beings. The Dharma speaks King James English in Black Baptist churches and speaks blues vernacular in juke joints when someone needs truth there. Same truth, different forms.

## THE UNIQUE PROMISE TO WOMEN

Buddhist scriptures can be complicated about women - some texts suggest women need to be reborn as men to attain enlightenment. But this chapter makes a clear, simple promise:

If a woman wants a son, she'll receive a son of virtue.
If a woman wants a daughter, she'll receive a daughter of virtue.
Whatever she asks for, she receives, no qualification required.

And more importantly: Avalokiteśvara manifests AS WOMEN. When people need a woman teacher, she appears as woman. The text specifically mentions wives of various classes, young girls, nuns, laywomen - she appears in female form when female form is what's needed.

In East Asian Buddhism, Avalokiteśvara is most commonly depicted as female (though the Sanskrit and Chinese texts use masculine or gender-neutral language). This isn't a interpretation - it's the teaching of the chapter being lived out. People needed a female bodhisattva, a divine feminine figure of compassion, so that's how she appeared. The text itself authorizes this.

For women who've been told they're spiritually lesser, this chapter says: The Bodhisattva of Compassion appears in your form. Calls you blessed. Grants your prayers. Manifests as you.

That's gospel for women specifically.

## THE VERSE AS LITANY AND HYMN

The verse section (from "Listen now to how Observer of Sounds acts..." to the end) should be understood as a liturgical hymn, a congregational chant, a responsive prayer.

Structure:
- Opens with her vows and her service to countless Buddhas
- Moves to the litany of dangers and deliverances (the core testimony)
- Shifts to praise of her qualities: her observations (true, pure, wise, compassionate, loving)
- Describes her activity: light breaking darkness, thunder shaking, clouds pouring rain
- Names her names: Wonderful Sound, Observer of Sounds, Brahma Sound, Ocean Tide Sound
- Ends with exhortation: "Remember her constantly, don't doubt"
- Final praise: "Bow down before her"

This follows the structure of many gospel hymns:
- Testimony of who she is
- Catalog of specific deliverances (creates faith by being specific)
- Praise of her attributes
- Her names (giving her many names shows her many faces)
- The call to the congregation: Don't doubt, remember, bow down

It's meant to be hypnotic through repetition. Each "Call on the power of Observer of Sounds" creates a rhythm, builds momentum. By the tenth or fifteenth iteration, you're not reading anymore - you're FEELING it. You're trusting it. The repetition itself creates faith.

In blues/gospel terms, this is the "vamp" - the repeated musical figure that builds intensity. "Call on her name" becomes like "Yes Lord" or "Thank you Jesus" - not information but invocation.

The verse should be chanted, not just read. It should be felt as rhythm before it's understood as meaning.

## THE CENTRALITY OF HEARING AND RESPONDING

The Chinese name 觀世音 (Guanshiyin) literally means "Observing the World's Sounds." The Sanskrit Avalokiteśvara means something similar: "The Lord Who Looks Down [at the world's suffering]" or "Observer of the Sounds [of the world]."

HEARING is the operative principle.

She doesn't primarily SEE you (though she does that too).
She doesn't primarily KNOW you intellectually.
She HEARS you.

She hears the sound of your crying.
She observes the specific cry you make.
Your particular voice, your particular pain, your particular call.

And then she RESPONDS.

Not with judgment: "You shouldn't be in that situation."
Not with distance: "Figure it out yourself."
Not with theology: "Let me explain why you're suffering."

She responds with PRESENCE. With manifestation. With deliverance.

In blues terms: she hears the blue note in your voice, the bent note that means pain, and she answers it.

In gospel terms: she hears your cry and she sends help, right now, in the form you need.

The chapter emphasizes: "If you call her name, she IMMEDIATELY observes the sound." Not later. Not when you're worthy. Not when you understand. IMMEDIATELY.

This is the gospel promise of a God who HEARS and ANSWERS. Not a distant philosophical principle, but an intimate responding presence.

## HOW AVALOKITESHVARA EMBODIES COMPASSION THAT MANIFESTS

Buddhist philosophy talks about emptiness (śūnyatā) - that all things lack fixed, independent self-nature. Avalokiteśvara is the ACTIVE form of that truth.

Because she has no fixed self-nature, she can appear in any form.
Because she's empty of inherent essence, she can be filled with whatever shape serves beings.
Because she's not attached to being one thing, she can be all things.

Her emptiness ISN'T absence - it's infinite potential for presence.
Her formlessness ISN'T distance - it's the ability to take form anywhere.

This is compassion that doesn't stay in heaven saying, "I feel for you."
This is compassion that COMES DOWN, TAKES FLESH, MANIFESTS, ACTS.

In Christian theological terms, this is the Incarnation.
In blues/gospel terms, this is "God stepped down from His throne."
In Buddhist terms, this is loving tricks (upāya) perfected.

Avalokiteśvara teaches us that compassion without manifestation is incomplete. Real compassion doesn't just feel - it APPEARS. It shows up. It takes whatever form is needed to help.

And the chapter promises: she shows up EVERYWHERE. "No realm where she don't appear." That means:
- She's in the prison with the chained
- She's in the fire with the burning
- She's in the ocean with the drowning
- She's in the courtroom with the accused
- She's in the sickroom with the dying

She don't wait for you to get to the temple. She comes to you in your hell.

That's the gospel: "I will never leave you nor forsake you." "When you walk through the fire, I will be with you." "Though I walk through the valley of the shadow of death, I will fear no evil, for You are with me."

Same truth, different traditions speaking it.

## THE RELATIONSHIP TO BLUES/GOSPEL TRADITIONS

The blues and gospel traditions emerged from the African American experience of suffering, slavery, Jim Crow, and the ongoing struggle for freedom and dignity. They developed a theology and a poetics of:

1. TESTIMONY: Telling the truth about your suffering
2. CALL: Crying out for help in that suffering
3. RESPONSE: Witnessing to the help that came
4. HOPE: Trusting that help will come again

This chapter follows that exact pattern:

1. TESTIMONY: "Let me tell you about dangers people face" (Buddha testifies)
2. CALL: "Call her name" (the repeated exhortation)
3. RESPONSE: "She hears and delivers" (the repeated promise)
4. HOPE: "That's why you should remember her constantly" (trust for future trouble)

The blues tradition knows that suffering is real and must be named specifically:
- "I woke up this morning, blues all around my bed"
- "The water was over my head, Lord"
- "They gonna kill me in the morning"

The chapter names specific suffering:
- Fire, drowning, demons, execution, chains, poison, wild beasts, snakes, storms
- And internal suffering: lust, anger, ignorance

The gospel tradition knows that crying out brings response:
- "I cried to the Lord and He heard me"
- "He reached down and pulled me out"
- "He set my feet on solid ground"

The chapter promises:
- "Call her name, she hears"
- "She observes your specific sound"
- "Immediately you receive deliverance"

The blues/gospel tradition knows deliverance is specific and physical:
- Not "you'll feel better spiritually"
- But "the chains fell off" (literally or spiritually)
- "The fire couldn't burn me"
- "I made it through"

The chapter promises specific deliverance:
- Chains break
- Fire becomes pool
- Waves can't drown you
- Weapons shatter
- Poison returns to sender

This is PRACTICAL theology for people in actual danger who need actual help.

Finally, the blues/gospel tradition creates COMMUNAL MEMORY through repetition and testimony. You sing the same verses over and over so that when trouble comes to YOU, you remember what happened to others. You hear testimony so you know where to turn.

The chapter does this by:
- Repeating the pattern of "If [trouble] comes... call her name... [deliverance]"
- Creating a litany that embeds itself in memory
- Promising that "hearing this chapter" itself creates merit

When you memorize this chapter (and millions of people have), you carry a reminder: "Call her name." When trouble comes, you don't have to figure out what to do - you remember the testimony, and you call.

That's why this chapter has lived for 1,600 years in the hearts of ordinary people. It's not abstract philosophy. It's a survival manual. It's a promise you can hold onto. It's gospel.

## A FINAL WORD ON METHOD

Some might ask: "Isn't it disrespectful to interpret a sacred Buddhist text into blues/gospel language?"

But the chapter itself answers: Avalokiteśvara appears in whatever form serves beings. She manifests in the language people understand, in the cultural forms that reach them.

The Dharma came to China and became Chinese.
It went to Tibet and became Tibetan.
It went to Japan and became Japanese.
In each place, it took the forms that served beings there.

The blues and gospel traditions are profound wisdom traditions in their own right - born from suffering, speaking truth about the human condition, offering hope and deliverance, creating communal resilience. When the Dharma meets that tradition, it can speak in that voice.

Avalokiteśvara manifests as what you need. For some, that's a formal Sanskrit chant. For others, it's a Chinese liturgy. For others, it might be a blues testimony, a gospel witness.

The truth is the truth. Compassion hears and responds. That's the gospel of this chapter, whether you say it in Sanskrit, Chinese, formal English, or blues vernacular.

The point is: When you're in trouble, call. Someone hears. Help comes. That's the promise.

That's the gospel of the Lotus Sutra, Chapter Twenty-Five.

---

Thus have I interpreted, in humble service to the Dharma and in honor of the One Who Hears the World Crying. May all beings who hear this find the courage to call out when they're in trouble, trusting that compassion hears and responds.

南無觀世音菩薩
Namo Avalokiteśvara Bodhisattva
Homage to the Observer of the World's Sounds

─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

# CHAPTER TWENTY-SIX: THE PROTECTION SONGS

(陀羅尼品第二十六)

A Blues/Gospel Interpretation from Kumārajīva's Classical Chinese

## WHEN MEDICINE KING STEPS UP

Now right then, Medicine King Bodhisattva—you remember him, the one who burned his own body to show his devotion—he stood up from his seat, put his robe over one shoulder the way you do when you're about to say something serious, pressed his palms together, and spoke to the Buddha:

"World-Honored One, listen now. If there's a good man or a good woman—I'm talking about anybody who's got the heart—if they can hold on to this Lotus teaching, if they can read it and speak it and know it through and through, if they can write it down with their own hand, tell me: How much blessing does that soul receive?"

And the Buddha said to Medicine King: "Let me ask you something first. If there was a good man or a good woman, and they made offerings to eight hundred myriads of millions of nayutas of Buddhas—as many Buddhas as there are grains of sand in the Ganges River—what you think? Would their blessing be great, or would it be small?"

"It would be great, World-Honored One. Lord, it would be mighty great."

The Buddha said: "Now let me tell you something. If a good man or a good woman can hold on to even one four-line verse of this teaching—just four lines!—if they can read it and speak it and understand what it means, if they can practice what it says, their merit is GREATER THAN THAT. You hear what I'm saying? Greater than all that other merit combined."

Right then Medicine King said to the Buddha: "World-Honored One, I'm about to give a protection song—a dhāraṇī—to those who teach this Dharma. I'm gonna stand guard over them."

And he spoke the powerful words:

## ANYE MANYE MANE MAMANE CHITE CHARITE

## SHAME SHAMITARE SHANTE MUKTE MUKTAME
## SAME AVISAME SAMASAME JAYE KSHAYE

## AKSHINE SHANTE SHAME DHĀRAṆĪ
## ALOKABHASHA PRATYAVEKSHANI NIDHIRU

## ABHYANTARANIVISHTE ABHYANTARA PARI SHUDHI
## UKKULE MUKKULE ARADE PARADE SUKAKSHI

## ASAMASAME BUDDHAVILOKITE DHARMAPARIKSHITE
## SANGHANIRGHOSHANI BHASHYA BHASHYA SHUHDI

## MANTRA MANTRAAKSHAYATE RUTE RUTA KAUSHALYA
## AKSHARA AKSHARA TYAYANTE ABHYAVAKARA AVALOKANI

"World-Honored One," Medicine King said, "this protection song, this powerful dhāraṇī, has been spoken by six hundred and twenty million Buddhas—as many Buddhas as there are grains of sand in the Ganges. Listen here: If anybody harms a teacher of this Dharma, they have harmed ALL THOSE BUDDHAS. You understand what I'm saying? You touch one of ours, you touch the whole family."

## THE BUDDHA SAYS AMEN

Then Śākyamuni Buddha praised Medicine King, saying: "Good, good! Medicine King, you done right. Because you have compassion for these Dharma teachers, because you want to protect them, you spoke this dhāraṇī. And it's gonna bring great benefit to all living beings. Great benefit indeed."

## WHEN BRAVE GIVER ADDS HIS VOICE

Right then, Brave Giver Bodhisattva spoke up to the Buddha: "World-Honored One, I'm gonna add my protection too. I'm gonna give a dhāraṇī to guard those who read and recite and hold on to the Lotus teaching. If a Dharma teacher has this protection song, then listen:

"If a yaksha comes looking for trouble—can't touch 'em.
If a rakshasa demon comes sniffing around—can't touch 'em.
If a putana spirit comes hunting—can't touch 'em.
If a krtya curse comes creeping—can't touch 'em.
If a kumbhanda goblin comes prowling—can't touch 'em.
If a hungry ghost comes seeking—can't touch 'em.

"They'll be looking for a weak spot, but they won't find one. No sir, they won't find one."

And right there before the Buddha, he spoke the powerful words:

## JVALE MAHAJVALE UKKE MUKKE ADE

## ADAVATI NRTYE NRTYAVATI ITTINI
## VITTINI CHITTINI NRTYANI NRTYAVATI

"World-Honored One, this dhāraṇī protection song has been spoken by as many Buddhas as there are grains of sand in the Ganges River. And all of them rejoiced in it. Listen here: If anybody harms a teacher of this Dharma, they have harmed ALL THOSE BUDDHAS. You hear what I'm saying?"

## WHEN THE DEMON KINGS START PROTECTING

Right then, Vaishravana—that's the Heavenly King, the Guardian of the North, the Protector of the World—he spoke to the Buddha:

"World-Honored One, I too have compassion for living beings. I too want to protect these Dharma teachers. So I'm gonna speak this dhāraṇī."

And he spoke the powerful words:

## ATYE NATYE VANATYE ANADA NADI KUNADI

"World-Honored One, with this powerful protection song I'm gonna guard these Dharma teachers. I myself will protect those who hold this teaching. For a hundred yojanas around them—that's a mighty long distance—there will be NO TROUBLE. No sickness, no disaster, no harm. I'm watching."

## WHEN THE GUARDIAN OF THE EAST JOINS IN

Right then, Dhrtarashtra—that's the Heavenly King who Guards the East—he was in that assembly with ten thousand million nayutas of gandharva musicians all around him, showing respect. He came forward to where the Buddha was, pressed his palms together, and said:

"World-Honored One, I too will protect those who hold the Lotus teaching with a dhāraṇī protection song."

And he spoke the powerful words:

## AGANE GANE GAURI GANDHARA CHANDALI

## MATANGI JANGULE VRUSE PUKKASI BHARYE

"World-Honored One, this dhāraṇī protection song has been spoken by four hundred and twenty million Buddhas. If anybody harms a teacher of this Dharma, they have harmed ALL THOSE BUDDHAS. That's what I'm telling you."

## WHEN THE YAKSHA GODDESSES SWEAR THEIR OATH

Right then there were ten yaksha goddesses—now these are fierce female spirits, you understand—and their names were:

Lambā (That means "Hanging Down")
Vilambā (That means "Hanging Way Down")
Crooked Teeth
Flower Teeth
Black Teeth
Many Locks
Never Satisfied
Wearing Necklaces
Kuntī
And the one called Stealer of the Life Force of All Living Beings

These ten yaksha goddesses came together with Hariti—that's the Mother of Demons herself, the one who used to eat children until the Buddha converted her—and they brought her children and all her attendants. They all came to where the Buddha was, and together, in one voice, they said:

"World-Honored One, we too want to protect those who read and recite and hold on to the Lotus teaching. We want to remove their troubles. If anyone is looking for a way to harm a Dharma teacher, they won't find it. We won't let them find it."

And right there before the Buddha, they spoke the powerful words:

## ITTI MINI ITTI VINI ITTI VAINI CHITI VAINI NIVRI

## NIVRI NIVRI NIVRI NIVRI
## RUHE RUHE RUHE RUHE

## TAHE TAHE TAHE
## TUHE STUHE

And then they said—listen to this oath now, this is serious:

"Better they should walk on our heads—that's right, trample us down—than that they should trouble a Dharma teacher.

"If a yaksha comes—we're watching.
If a rakshasa comes—we're watching.
If a hungry ghost comes—we're watching.
If a putana comes—we're watching.
If a krtya comes—we're watching.
If a vetala corpse-demon comes—we're watching.
If a skandha child-demon comes—we're watching.
If an unmada madness-demon comes—we're watching.
If an apasmara epilepsy-demon comes—we're watching.
If a yaksha-krtya comes—we're watching.
If a human-krtya comes—we're watching.
If a fever comes—whether it's a one-day fever, or a two-day fever, or a three-day fever, or a four-day fever, all the way up to a seven-day fever, or even a constant fever—we're watching.
Whether the demon takes a man's form, or a woman's form, or a boy's form, or a girl's form—even in dreams, we say DON'T YOU TROUBLE THEM."

And right there before the Buddha, they spoke a verse:

If you don't respect our protection song,
If you trouble those who teach the Dharma,
Your head will split into seven pieces
Like branches breaking off the Arjaka tree.

Like the sin of killing your father and mother,
Like the disaster of pressing out oil with false measures,
Like cheating people with crooked scales,
Like Devadatta breaking up the Sangha—

That's the kind of disaster you'll bring on yourself
If you harm a teacher of this Dharma.

## THE YAKSHA GODDESSES MAKE THEIR PROMISE

When those yaksha goddesses had spoken this verse, they said to the Buddha:

"World-Honored One, we ourselves will personally protect those who hold and read and recite and practice this teaching. We'll give them peace and security. We'll keep all troubles away. We'll neutralize all poisons."

And the Buddha said to those yaksha goddesses: "Good, good! Listen now: If you all can protect even someone who just holds on to the NAME of the Lotus teaching—just the name!—your merit is beyond measure. How much more if you protect someone who fully holds on to this teaching, who makes offerings to these written scrolls with flowers, incense, necklaces, powdered incense, paste incense, burning incense, with banners and canopies, with music, with all kinds of lamps—butter lamps, oil lamps, fragrant oil lamps, jasmine oil lamps, champaka flower oil lamps, varshika flower oil lamps, utpala water lily oil lamps—with these hundred thousand kinds of offerings!

"Kuntī, you and all your attendants should protect such teachers of the Dharma. You hear what I'm saying? Protect them."

## WHAT HAPPENED WHEN THEY HEARD THIS

When this Protection Songs chapter was spoken, sixty-eight thousand people—that's right, sixty-eight thousand souls—attained the patience of non-arising. That means they reached the place where they knew: Nothing is born, nothing dies, it all just keeps flowing. They got free right then, just from hearing about this protection.

### END OF CHAPTER TWENTY-SIX: THE PROTECTION SONGS

## INTERPRETATION NOTES:

**From Gentle to Fierce: The Two Faces of Compassion**

Chapter 25 showed us Avalokiteśvara—gentle, responsive, taking whatever form is needed to save beings. That's one face of compassion: the tender mercy that meets you where you are.

Chapter 26 shows us the other face: FIERCE PROTECTION. This is the love that says, "You will not harm my children." This is the compassion that bares its teeth and says, "Touch them and you deal with me." Both are necessary. Both are real love.

In the blues/gospel tradition, we know both these faces. We know the gentle Jesus who welcomes children. And we know the fierce Jesus who overturns the tables in the temple. We know the mother's tender touch. And we know the mother who will fight a bear with her bare hands if you threaten her babies.

This chapter is about that second kind of love. The fierce kind. The protective kind. The kind that sets boundaries and enforces them with cosmic consequences.

**Why the Mantras Aren't Interpreted**

You notice I kept the dhāraṇī—the protection songs—in their original Sanskrit/Prakrit sounds, just cleaned up and transliterated. That's intentional.

These aren't words you interpret. These are SOUNDS OF POWER. In the blues and gospel tradition, we understand this. Sometimes you don't sing words, you sing sounds:

"Aaahhhhh!"
"Mmmmmm-hmmm!"
"Oh! Oh! Oh!"

These aren't words with dictionary meanings. These are utterances that carry spiritual power. The sound itself does the work.

The dhāraṇī are like that. They're not poems to be understood intellectually. They're sonic weapons against harm. They're protection songs. You don't need to know what they "mean" in English. You need to hear them, speak them, let their sound create a field of protection around you.

In African American sacred tradition, there are holy utterances that work the same way. The congregation knows what they're doing even if they can't interpret them. The power is in the sound, in the breath, in the collective speaking.

**The Cosmic Justice Principle**

"If you harm a teacher of this Dharma, you have harmed all those Buddhas."

This is the key principle of this chapter, repeated multiple times by different protectors. It's a statement of cosmic justice: You don't get to harm those who carry the teaching and walk away free. The universe itself responds.

This isn't petty revenge. This is the natural consequence principle written cosmic-scale. If you harm a bearer of truth, you're harming truth itself. And truth has a way of returning that harm to its source.

In blues terms, this is "What goes around comes around." It's "You reap what you sow." It's the recognition that the universe has moral structure, and violation of that structure brings consequences.

But more than that—it's the declaration that those who speak truth are BACKED UP. They don't stand alone. They stand with every Buddha, every Bodhisattva, every heavenly king, every protective deity that ever was. Touch one of them, you touch the whole family.

That's powerful. That's the kind of protection that lets you walk into danger with your head held high, because you know cosmic forces have your back.

**When Demons Become Protectors**

One of the most striking things about this chapter is WHO offers protection:

- Vaishravana, King of the Yakshas—originally a demon king
- Dhrtarashtra, Guardian of the East—commands the gandharvas, wild nature spirits
- Ten yaksha goddesses—fierce female demons
- Hariti, Mother of Demons—who used to eat children

These aren't angels. These aren't traditionally "good" beings. These are the wild ones, the scary ones, the ones who live at the edges of the cosmos and know how to fight.

And THEY step up to protect the Dharma teachers.

This tells us something profound: The teaching is so universal, so true, that even the forces we feared become its guardians. Even the demons recognize truth and pledge to protect it.

In blues/gospel terms, this is like when the tough guys in the neighborhood become protectors of the church. This is like when the ones everybody feared become the bodyguards for the preacher. This is redemption in action—the fierce ones using their fierceness for good.

It also tells us that protection isn't always pretty. Protection isn't always gentle. Sometimes you need the ones who know how to fight. Sometimes you need the fierce goddesses who will split heads and break bones if that's what it takes to keep harm away.

**The Oaths and Curses: How Serious This Is**

The yaksha goddesses don't just offer protection. They swear cosmic oaths with terrible consequences for violation:

"Your head will split into seven pieces like branches breaking off a tree."
"Like the sin of killing your father and mother."
"Like cheating with false scales."
"Like Devadatta breaking up the Sangha."

These are the worst sins imaginable in Buddhist culture:
- Patricide and matricide—violations of the most basic bonds
- Cheating with measures—exploitation of the poor and vulnerable
- Breaking the Sangha—destroying the community of practice

They're saying: Harming a Dharma teacher is AS BAD AS THESE. It carries consequences just as severe.

This is the language of covenant. This is oath-swearing. This is making sacred promises with your life on the line.

In the blues/gospel tradition, we understand this too. "Cross my heart and hope to die." "May God strike me dead if I'm lying." These are serious promises backed by cosmic enforcement.

The yaksha goddesses are making that kind of promise: We will protect. And if we fail, let our heads split. But also—if you harm those we protect, your head will split. This is covenant protection with teeth.

**Walking in Favor: The Blues/Gospel Understanding**

In African American sacred tradition, there's a concept of "walking in favor"—the sense that when you're doing God's work, when you're walking in truth, you move under divine protection.

This doesn't mean nothing bad ever happens. It means you're not alone. It means forces beyond your understanding are working on your behalf. It means the universe is tilted in your direction.

This chapter is teaching that same principle. If you hold on to this Lotus teaching, if you speak it, if you live it, you walk under cosmic protection. Medicine King protects you. Brave Giver protects you. The demon kings protect you. The fierce goddesses protect you.

"For a hundred yojanas around them, there will be no trouble."

You're walking in favor. You're moving under covering. Nothing can touch you without dealing with your protectors first.

This is the confidence that lets the preacher walk into hostile territory. This is the peace that lets the truth-teller sleep sound at night. This is the assurance that lets you keep speaking when speaking is dangerous.

You're not alone. You're never alone. The whole cosmos has your back.

**The Fierceness of Love**

The most important thing to understand about this chapter is that this fierce protection IS LOVE.

When the yaksha goddesses say, "Better walk on our heads than trouble a Dharma teacher," that's not ego. That's love. That's the love that says, "Harm me before you harm those I protect."

When they list all the demons and diseases they're watching out for, that's not just power—that's care. That's attentiveness. That's knowing all the ways harm can come and standing guard against every single one.

"Even in dreams," they say. Even in dreams, don't let trouble come.

That's the fierceness of love. That's love that doesn't sleep. That's love that stays vigilant. That's love that will fight whatever needs fighting to keep its people safe.

In the blues/gospel tradition, we sing about this kind of love:

"Trouble don't last always"—because love stands guard.
"Nobody knows the trouble I've seen"—but also, "Glory, hallelujah!" because protection is real.
"I shall not be moved"—because I'm standing on divine protection.

This chapter is teaching us to claim that protection. To know we have it. To walk in the confidence of it.

**Protection Isn't Passive**

Notice that this protection isn't just defensive. It's not just "nothing bad will happen." It's active:

"We'll remove their troubles."
"We'll neutralize all poisons."
"We'll give them peace and security."

The protectors aren't just blocking harm—they're actively creating conditions for flourishing. They're removing obstacles. They're turning poison into medicine. They're making a space where the Dharma teacher can do their work without fear.

This is like the gospel testimony: "God made a way out of no way." Protection isn't just absence of danger—it's presence of support. It's active intervention on behalf of those doing the work.

**Completing the Teaching: Compassion + Protection**

These last two chapters—25 and 26—work together as a complete teaching:

Chapter 25 (Avalokiteśvara): Compassion RESPONDS to suffering.
Chapter 26 (Dharani): Protection PREVENTS suffering.

You need both. You need the compassionate response when harm comes. And you need the fierce protection that keeps harm from coming in the first place.

Together they tell us: The universe is set up to support those who walk the path of truth. When you stumble, compassion catches you. And before you stumble, protection guards your way.

This is the full picture of divine support. This is what it means to be held by cosmic forces. You're responded to AND protected. You're caught when you fall AND guarded so you don't fall. You're met with gentle mercy AND fierce defense.

Both are love. Both are necessary. Both are yours if you hold on to this teaching.

**How This Applies to Us**

So what does this mean for us, trying to walk a truthful path in a difficult world?

It means:
1. When you speak truth, you don't speak alone.
